The following action was taken by the General Assembly:
"6. That the Ad-interim Committee to Discuss . . . be continued for one year, and that in the event

<a id="ga08-p15"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=15 printed_page=null -->

DIRECTORY 13

approaches from any other Churches are made to the PCA during the coming year, the Ad-interim
Committee be authorized to welcome, receive and study such approaches; be directed to communi
cate such information to the Church-at-large all means available: and report to the Committee of
Commissioners on Interchurch Relations at the Ninth General Assembly of the PCA.
"7. In response to Communication 2 from the 47th General Assembly of the Orthodox Presbyterian
Church, the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America take the following
actions:

- **a.** That the Ad-interim Committee continue to work on its original mandate, and that they meet with the representatives of the OPC. and of the RPCES and RPCNA, if the latter so desires, to draw up a statement that exhibits the representatives' understanding (or, if necessary, individual statements that exhibit individual understandings) of the compatibility of the participating Churches, the statement to take into consideration discussion of those questions raised by PCA representatives at the joint meeting held September 14, 1979, and any other pertinent issues.
- **b.** That the Ad-interim Committee be instructed to report by means of a letter to all teaching elders and clerks of session no latter than February 1, 1981. areas of similarity and difference among the PCA, OPC, RPCES and RPCNA, giving a brief summary of each Church's position on these areas based on their standards and assembly pronouncements, along with a description of the size and location of the individual churches of each denomination.
- **c.** That the Ad-interim Committee report to the Ninth General Assembly of the PCA through the

Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations their recommendations as to future
efforts in the area of Church unity." §8-43 pp 83-84
AD HOC COMMITTEE TO STUDY PCA FOUNDATION
The Moderator of the Eighth General Assembly, Paul G. Settle, announced the appointment of the following
members to serve as the Ad Hoc Committee to Study the PCA Foundation:
Committee Name
Administration James W. Lipscomb, Louisiana
John Culver, Gulf Coast
Christian Education and Publications William Huffman, Eastern Carolina
Paul Kooistra. Warrior
Mission to the United States Robert Cannada, Jr.. Covenant
Logan Porter. Eastern Carolina
Mission to the World Donald Comer, Central Georgia
Charles Young, Warrior
Stewardship Stuart Perrin, Ascension, Convener
Gerald Sovereign, Gulf Coast
PCA Foundation Laurie V. Jones, Covenant
Steve A. White. Eastern Carolina
' 4 That an ad hoc committee be appointed by the moderator of the General Assembly, two members
from each of the Committees of the General Assembly, two members of the Subcommittee on
Stewardship, and two members of the trustees of the PCA Foundation The purpose of the
committee will be to study the proposed plan for operation of PCA Foundation as outlined for the
Eighth General Assembly and to report to the Ninth General Assembly through the Committee of
Commissioners of PCA Foundation. That each committee and sub-committee bear the expense of
its representatives. This committee to give particular attention to the following specific issues:

- **a.** Whether Foundation activities be restricted to receiving, accumulation, managing, investing and disbursing capital funds, stocks, property, etc.
- **b.** If the Foundation should also be allowed to solicit funds, gifts, bequests, etc.
- **c.** To consider the relationship of the Foundation to the Sub-committee on Stewardship and to the four permanent committees.
- **d.** Whether the Foundation should have a full-time director, and if so. what should his qualifica tions and duties be.

5. That the ad hoc committee develop and present to the Ninth General Assembly a plan to place the
operation of the PCA Foundation under the rules for General Assembly operation and bylaws "
§ 8-79, pp. 107-108.

# JOURNAL MINUTES — MONDAY AFTERNOON

June 16, 1980

## First Session

### 8-1 The Assembly Called to Order

The Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America, meeting in the Civic Center Auditorium, Savannah, Georgia, hosted by the churches of Central Georgia Presbytery, was called to order at 1:00 p.m., June 16, 1980, by Moderator William F. Joseph, Jr., who led the Assembly in an opening prayer. Following the singing of a hymn, the moderator introduced a season of prayer, calling to the Assembly’s attention the death of Past Moderator Leon F. Hendrick and the roll of teaching elders deceased since the last Assembly.

|  Name | Presbytery | Deceased  |
| --- | --- | --- |
|  Nam Chin Cha | Pacific | July 1979  |
|  Dan H. McCown | Texas | August 1979  |
|  Vernon A. Crawford | Calvary | October 1979  |
|  Eugene Koller | Gulf Coast | March 1980  |
|  Thomas L. Llewelyn | Mississippi Valley | April 1980  |

TE William G. Hughes began and TE Robert J. Ostenson concluded the season of prayer. Moderator Joseph then exhorted the Assembly, using as his text I John 4:7ff. TE Robert L. Craggs and TE A. Dale Umbreit led the Assembly in celebrating the Sacrament of the Lord’s Supper, with the assistance of ruling elders of the Assembly and the Presbytery of Central Georgia. The moderator declared a fifteen minute recess at 2:35 p.m.

### 8-2 Greetings from Mayor of Savannah

The Assembly reconvened at 2:50 p.m., and, as a matter of personal privilege, Moderator Joseph introduced the Honorable John P. Rousakis, mayor of Savannah, who welcomed the Assembly to the city.

### 8-3 Report on Enrollment

Stated Clerk Morton H. Smith announced that a quorum was present. The final enrollment of commissioners was as follows:

8-4 Election of Moderator
Five teaching elders were nominated for the office of moderator: Todd W. Allen,
B. I. Anderson, Donald C. Graham, O. Palmer Robertson, and Paul G. Settle. TE
Paul G. Settle was elected on the first ballot.

### A. COMMUNICATIONS TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY

To the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures
Communication 1: From The Fairfield Church, Fairton, New Jersey
(Ordinarily communications are not received directly from congregations but due to the special nature of this
letter it is printed for the information of the genera i Assembly.)
March 25, 1980
Dr. Morton Smith, Stated Clerk,
Commissioners to the Eighth General Assembly, and
Members of the Presbyterian Church in America
Dear Friends in Christ,
By 1680, Puritans from the area surrounding Fairfield, Conn. had settled on the shores of the Delaware
Bay and had gathered themselves together as a congregation of believers in the Lord Jesus Christ. "Christ's
Church at Fairfield” became a part of America's first Presbytery (in Philadelphia) by 1708.
We, the spiritual descendants of those Godly men and women, members of the congregation which they
gathered in this place, are this year giving thanks to God for His gracious care over the Fairfield Presbyterian
Church for these 300 years. He has faithfully provided ministers of the Word. Noteworthy among these was the
work of Ethan Osborn, pastor of this church for 55 years (1789-1844), God's instrument in six waves of revival
in the early nineteenth century.
In this year of celebration for us in the Fairfield Presbyterian Church, we invite congregations, officers,
and members of the PCA to add their voices to ours in praise of the Lord of the Church whose mercy has
preserved the witness of truth in this place for three centuries. We cordially extend an invitation to each of you

<a id="ga08-p31"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=31 printed_page=null -->

to be present with us on September 21, 1980, for our tricentennial observances. At 10:00 AM an historical
communion service will be held in our "Old Stone Church," (erected in 1780). At 4:00 PM former pastors,
dignitaries, and friends will bring greetings in a service of praise in our present sanctuary (erected in 1850).
We trust that you will join us in prayer, if not by your presence, in this, our tricentennial thanksgiving.
Sincerely, in Christ’s service,
Lawrence C. Roff, Moderator
For the Session of the
Fairfield Presbyterian Church
Fairton, New Jersey
Answered § 8-69, III; 5, p. 99.
To the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations
Communication 2: From the Committee on Ecumenicity and Interchurch Relations of the
Orthodox Presbyterian Church
action of the 47th (1980) General Assembly of the orthodox presbyterian church in re merger of the OPC.
PC A . RPCES. and RPCNA.
That the Assembly affirm its desire to achieve biblical unity and union with the Presbyterian Church in America, the Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, and the Reformed Presbyterian Church of
North America as soon as possible;
That in view of this desire, and in the light of the meeting held September 14, 1979, the Assembly
fraternally request the 1980 General Assembly/Synods of the above-named churches to concur with us in the
following proposals:
1. That there be a meeting of representatives of the four churches at an early time after their 1980 major
assemblies for the following purposes:

- **a.** To draw up a statement that exhibits the representatives' joint understanding or, if necessary, individual statements that exhibit an individual understanding, of the compatibility of these participating churches, the statement to take into consideration discussion of those questions raised by the PCA representatives at the joint meeting held September 14, 1979;
- **b.** to ensure insofar as possible that if a united church were to be achieved it would produce a church of one mind in its willingness to deal on a biblical basis with issues that would inevitably arise from time to time, which would, in turn, minimize the possibility of division in the future;
- **c.** To recommend to the participating churches, on the basis of the statement, or statements, what course they should follow with respect to achieving a united church; and

2. That the PCA representatives be requested to convene the joint meeting;
3. That following the joint meeting, the statement and recommendations be reported to the 1981
General Assemblies/Synods of the participating churches;
4. That if the joint meeting decides to make a recommendation that would have in view the possibility
of merger, the standards of government, discipline, and worship of the respective churches
participating in the recommendation should be provided for each session and minister of these
churches in as economical a form as possible, the total cost to be met by establishing a per copy
charge and. if necessary, also apportioning a part of the cost among the participating denominations
on a per capita communicant member basis; and that the Committee on Ecumenicity and Inter
church Relations be instructed to inform the sessions and ministers of our church what differences
there may be between the Confession of Faith and Larger and Shorter Catechisms of the Orthodox
Presbyterian Church, on the one hand and, on the other hand, the form of the Confessions of Faith
and Larger and Shorter Catechisms held by the participating churches; and
5. That this General Assembly respectfully inform the 1980 General Assembly of the PCA and the
General Synods of the RPCES and RPCNA that it is our opinion that the interests of the unity of the
body of Christ would be served well by holding in abeyance formal consideration of merger until
the major assembly meetings of 1981 when there shall have been opportunity for each church to
receive the information it needs in order to act on a matter of such far-reaching effect upon all our
members and churches.
6. That the Assembly instruct its Committee on Ecumenicity and Interchurch Relations ( I) to convey
the action requesting a joint meeting of the PCA, the RPCES, and the RPCNA at the earliest
possible time before the 1980 General Assembly of the PCA, and (2) to consult with the
representatives of these churches in making arrangements for the meeting, and (3) if the meeting is
held, to participate in it and to present to the sessions and ministers of the Orthodox Presbyterian
Church as soon as possible after the meeting, and to the next General Assembly (1981), a careful
evaluation of the meeting, of its conclusions, and of any statement and/or recommendations by the
joint meeting
Answered § 8-43, IV, 7, p. 83.

<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=32 printed_page=null -->

### B. OVERTURES TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY

To the Committee of Commissioners on Administration

##### Overture 5: From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the Committee on Administration of the Presbyterian Church in America has decided against
pursuing the possibility of a meeting of the General Assembly in Pittsburgh in 1982; and

Whereas, the specific reason for this decision was the potential embarrassment to the dignity and the
integrity of the PCA's relationship to the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America, a Church which
shares with the PCA membership in the North American Presbyterian and Reformed Council and whose
facilities the PCA would have been using at the very time that Church would have been meeting in Grand
Rapids, Michigan, with the other Churches in NAP ARC; and

Whereas, both proper decorum and courtesy would suggest that the PCA should honor its commitment
to practice fellowship with the Churches in NAPARC; and

Whereas, new developments have surfaced in the relationship enjoyed between the PCA and the
Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, the Orthodox Presbyterian Church and the Reformed
Presbyterian Church of North America, as a result of which a concurrent meeting of general assemblies and
General Synods would seem to be most useful at this time; and

Whereas, the travel distance does not seem to be a prohibitive consideration, it being farther from
Jackson, Mississippi, to Fort Lauderdale, Florida, where the Assembly is scheduled to meet in 1981, than it is
from Jackson to Grand Rapids;

Now Therefore, Be It Resolved, that the Presbytery of Warrior does overture the General Assembly
to reconsider its decision on the site of the 1982 General Assembly meeting, with a view of joining the other
denominations in NAPARC in Grand Rapids.
Attested:
T.E. FredrickS. Carr
Stated Clerk
15 January 1980
Answered in the affirmative. § 8-103, III, 2, p. 121.

##### Overture 13: From the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida

(Note: This Overture was presented to Gulf Coast Presbytery, but was not adopted by Presbytery.)

Whereas, the Reformed Presbyterian Church. North America, the denomination owning and controlling
Geneva College, Beaver, Pennsylvania, has committed to meet jointly with the other members of the North
American Presbyterian and Reformed Council at Calvin College in Grand Rapids, Michigan in 1982;

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America maintains fraternal relations with the other members
meeting at Calvin College, Grand Rapids, Michigan in 1982;

Whereas, we believe that to deliberately meet elsewhere might well give the impression of boycotting
the North American Presbyterian and Reformed Council;

Therefore, the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida overtures the
General Assembly to request the Committee on Administration to re-consider and revise the plans for the 1982
General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America so that said General Assembly meets concurrently
with the other North American Presbyterian and Reformed Council members at Calvin College in Grand
Rapids, Michigan in 1982.
Adopted by the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida on November
19. 1979.
Attested:
M.C. Hull
Clerk of Session
C. Don Darling
Moderator of Session
Answered in the affirmative. § 8-103, III, 2, p. 121.

##### Overture 21: From the Presbytery of Central Florida

Whereas, each year the Permanent Judicial Committee receives many requests to assist presbyteries and
sessions in interpreting various portions of our Book of Church Order, and

Whereas, the complaints and appeals in cases of judicial process with which the General Assembly has
had to deal each year give evidence of the difficulties presbyteries and sessions have in making proper
application of our Book of Church Order, now.

Therefore, the Presbytery of Central Florida overtures the General Assembly to instruct the Stated Clerk
to prepare a Digest of Assembly Actions taken which provide guidance in the interpretation and application of
our Book of Church Order, this digest to be prepared in loose-leaf form, fully indexed and annotated as
appropriate to its use, to be updated annually.
Further, it is requested that the Stated Clerk be granted the services of an assistant for a term of one

<a id="ga08-p33"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=33 printed_page=null -->

man-month in the initial preparation of this digest if, in his judgment, such assistance is necessary.
Adopted at the meeting of Presbytery, January 15, 1980.
Charles U. Ambler, Jr.
Stated Clerk
Answered in the affirmative. § 8-103, III, 15, p. 123.

##### Overture 24: From Louisiana Presbytery

Whereas, the task of Christ's Elders is the ministry of His Word and Prayer (Acts 6:4) and

Whereas, Christ is the sovereign king who rules and guides His Church (Ephesians 4:5),

Therefore, we recommend that at least two hours per day be devoted each day of General Assembly to
Bible study, prayer, and preaching.
Adopted at Spring Stated Meeting of Louisiana Presbytery, March 15, 1980.
Attest:
BakerS. Smith, Stated Clerk
Louisiana Presbytery
Answered in the negative. § 8-103, III, 16, p. 123.

##### Overture 25: From Louisiana Presbytery

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America strives for a parity between Elders who rule and Elders who
teach, and

Whereas, Ruling Elders often are frustrated by the large number of registered Teaching Elders who vote at
General Assembly and Committee of Commissioner's Committees, and

Whereas, the maturity and counsel of Elders who rule is vital and yet often over-shadowed by the number
of Teaching Elders eligible and present.

Therefore, we propose that a ratio between the registered Ruling Elders and Teaching Elders be
established each General Assembly and in each Committee of Commissioner's Committee and the minority
Elders vote shall be increased in all General Assembly and Committee of Commissioner's Committees voting
activity in order to arrive at a voting equality.
Adopted at Spring Stated Meeting of Louisiana Presbytery. March 15. 1980.
Attest:
Baker S. Smith, Stated Clerk
Louisiana Presbytery
Answered in the negative. § 8-103, III. 17 p. 123.

To the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures

##### Overture 2: From the Presbytery of Mississippi Valley

Whereas, the General Assembly, as a court of jesus Christ, should speak with a united voice in
affirming the sanctity of human life under the protection of the Sixth Commandment,

Therefore Be It Resolved, that Mississippi Valley Presbytery overture the Eighth General Assembly to
reaffirm its original statement on abortion:
"That because Scripture clearly affirms the sanctity of human life and condemns its arbituary destruc
tion, we affirm that the intentional killing of an unborn child between conception and birth, for any
reason at any time, is clearly a violation of the Sixth Commandment."
Added to this statement are the following affirmations:
"Concerning crisis pregnancies in which it appears that the premature removal of the unborn child from
the mother is a necessary consequence of medical procedures essential to preserving the mother's life, we
affirm that:
1. The Sixth Commandment not only forbids the taking of innocent life for whatever reason but also
requires the preserving of innocent life wherever possible.
2. The life of the mother as well as her child comes under the full protection of the Sixth Command
ment and all moral medical wisdom and skill must be used to preserve her life as well as the life of
her child.
3. To say that we are ever placed in the position of choosing between two sins (killing the child or
neglecting the preservation of the mother's life) is to surrender our belief in the Sovereign
overruling providence of our All-wise and All-holy God (I Cor. 10:13) and to allege that we must
"do evil that good may come", a philosophy clearly condemned by Scripture.
4. In the extremely rare case in which in the judgment of competent medical authorities, the unborn
child's continuing presence inside the mother's body will necessarily lead to the mother's death, the
premature removal of the unborn child may be justified, provided that all medical wisdom,
judgment, and skill are used to preserve the life of the child as well as the life of the mother. And at
that juncture of time where the greatest possibility for recovery is indicated for both mother and
child. If life is lost in such a case, and the death occurs not out of criminal negligence, but merely
out of limitations of human knowledge and skill, all has been done morally that could be done. If we
cannot save both lives, we are nevertheless morally bound to save the life we can."
Adopted at the Stated Meeting of Presbytery, October 16, 1979.
Attest:
Thomas A. Cook
Stated Clerk
Answered by reference to answer to Overture 12. § 8-69, III, 3; p. 98.

##### Overture 7: From Grace Presbytery

Whereas, the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America, a court of the Church of Jesus
Christ, should speak with a clarion voice in affirming the truth of the Word of God and the application of that
Word to life; and

Whereas, the Seventh General Assembly did enact an amendment to the statement on abortion adopted
by the Sixth General Assembly, which, as adopted, is ambiguous. The ambiguity exists because the
amendment admits that the "intentional killing of an unborn child between conception and birth (abortion)" in
one excepted specified circumstance may not be a violation of the Sixth Commandment and, yet, directs that
"all possible efforts are to be made to preserve the lives of both the mother and the child" (emphasis added);
and

Whereas, the General Assembly is agreed that the Scriptures affirm the sanctity of life;

Therefore, Be It Resolved, that Grace Presbytery overture the Eighth General Assembly of the
Presbyterian Church in America to rescind the amendment adopted by the Seventh General Assembly; to
reaffirm the statement on abortion adopted by the Sixth General Assembly; and to amend that statement by the
addition of the following:
In those cases in which it is the judgment of competent medical authorities that the continued presence of
the unborn child within the mother's body is a certain threat to the life of the mother, the premature
removal of the unborn child may be justified provided that the procedure shall not involve intentional
aborticide and that all possible medical procedures are used to preserve the life of the child as well as the
life of the mother.
Adopted at the 25th Stated Meeting of Grace Presbytery, January 11, 1980.
Attest:
Rev. Norman A. Bagby, Jr.
Stated Clerk
Answered by reference to answer to Overture 12. § 8-69, III, 3; p. 98.

##### Overture 11: From the Presbytery of Eastern Carolina

Whereas, an overture brought before the 1979 General Assembly on the subject of alcoholic beverages
was not received by the Assembly; (Minutes, p. 92); and

Whereas, the General Assembly of 1979 rejected the ruling of the Sub-committee on Judicial Business

<a id="ga08-p35"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=35 printed_page=null -->

that the overture was in order; (Minutes, p. 181); and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order 15-6 authorizes the General Assembly to "recommend measures
for the promotion of charity, truth, and holiness through all the churches under its care"; and

Whereas, the consumption of alcoholic beverages is one of the greatest hindrances to holiness in our
land; and

Whereas, the Scripture view of Christian liberty is clearly stated in Romans 14:21, 1 Corinthians 8:13,
and especially in 1 Peter 2:16; and

Whereas, the consumption of alcoholic beverages continues to be one of the most serious stumbling
blocks in our country today;

Be It Resolved, by the General Assembly in an in ihesi deliverance that total abstinance from alcoholic
beverages, except in medicinal use, be the approved position of our denomination in this matter.
Adopted by Eastern Carolina Presbytery on Jan 26, 1980.
Attest:
C. Gene Pjrks
Stated Clerk
Answered in the negative, with comment. § 8-69, 111, 4; p. 98.

##### Overture 12: From Evangel Presbytery

Whereas, the General Assembly, as a court of jesus Christ, should speak with a united voice in
affirming the sanctity of human life under the protection of the Sixth Commandment,

Therefore Be It Resolved, that Evangel Presbytery overture the Eighth General Assembly to reaffirm its

"That because Scripture clearly affirms the sanctity of human life and condemns its arbitrary destruction,
we affirm that the intentional killing of an unborn child between conception and birth, for any reason at
any time, is clearly a violation of the Sixth Commandment. "
Added to this statement are the following affirmations:
"Concerning crisis pregnancies in which it appears that the premature removal of the unborn child from
the mother is a necessary consequence of medical procedures essential to preserving the mother's life, we
affirm that:
I The Sixth Commandment not only forbids the taking of innocent life for whatever reason, but also
requires the preserving of innocent life wherever possible,
2. The life of the mother as well as her child comes under the full protection of the Sixth Command
ment and all moral medical wisdom and skill must be used to preserve her life as well as the life of
her child.
3. To say that we are ever placed in the position of choosing between two sins (killing the child or
neglecting the preservation of the mother's life) is to surrender our belief in the Sovereign
overruling providence of our All-wise and All-holy God (1 Cor. 10:13) and to allege that we must
' do evil that good may come” . . a philosophy clearly condemned by Scripture.
4 An exception is not made even in the extremely rare case in which in the judgment of competent
medical authorities, the unborn child’s continuing presence inside the mother's body will necessar
ily lead to the mother's death, the premature removal of the unborn child may be justified, provided
that all medical wisdom, judgment, and skill are used to preserve the life of the child as well as the
life of the mother. This premature removal of the unborn child shall be at that juncture of time where
the greatest possibility for recovery is indicated for both mother and child. If life is lost in such a
case, and the death occurs not out of criminal negligence, but merely out of the limitations of human
knowledge and skill, all has been done morally that could be done. If we cannot save both lives, we
are nevertheless morally bound to save the life we can. "
Adopted this 22nd day of January, 1980, in meeting at the Oak Park Presbyterian Church, Montgomery,
Alabama.

Hubert C. Stewart

##### Overture 27: From the Presbytery of the Ascension

Whereas, the Sixth General Assembly was of one mind in recognizing that the unborn child is a person
from the moment of conception; and

Whereas, such persons, being created in the image of God, are entitled to the full protection of the law of
God in the Sixth Commandment; and

Whereas, the Westminster Larger Catechism. Question 136. rightly specifies the only Scriptural excep
tions to the prohibition of taking life, namely capital punishment, lawful war, and necessary defense; and

Whereas, an unborn child is (a) incapable of committing a capital offense, (b) incapable of the aggression
which legitimates killing in self-defense (unless [a] is denied), and (c) abortion is not a proper activity of lawful
war, that is, it is senseless to declare war on a fetus or view it as a warring enemy; and

Whereas, the action of the Seventh General Assembly which erected a new, fourth exception to the Sixth
Commandment (a) was not given on Scriptural grounds but rather reasons of emotion spd expediency and (b)
implicitly denies the unborn child's status as a person created in God's image by denying him the God-given

<a id="ga08-p36"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=36 printed_page=null -->

protection to all persons, thus contradicting the Scriptural foundation of the Ad-Interim Committee Report and
thereby contradicting the basis of prohibiting abortion for other reasons as well; and

Whereas, the pretext for such a revision was that the assembly was divided, a position which if
consistently followed would annul virtually all other assembly actions since they ordinarily carry some
negative vote; and

Whereas, some who voted with the majority did not realize they were altering the General Assembly
position but thought they were merely observing that the vote was divided; and

Whereas, the revision in no way strengthened our testimony to the obligation to use all legitimate means
to preserve the life of the mother as well as the child; and

Whereas, the last sentence which was added to the Seventh General Assembly’s action contradicts what
precedes it, since one cannot take "all possible efforts" to preserve the life of the child when abortion is
permitted in some cases; and

Whereas, the blatant devaluing of the life of unborn children is so rampant in our society, pointing to the
need for strict adherence to Scripture alone;

Therefore, be it resolved that the Presbytery of the Ascension overtures the Eighth General Assembly to
affirm without equivocation the action of the Sixth General Assembly, namely,
"That because Scripture clearly affirms the sanctity of human life and condemns its arbitrary
destruction, we affirm that the intentional killing of an unborn child between conception and birth,
for any reason at any time, is clearly a violation of the Sixth Commandment.
Adopted the eighth day of January, 1980, at Akron, Oh
Frank D. Moser, Stated Clerk
Answered by reference to answer to Overture 12. § 8-69, III, 3; p. 98.

##### Overture 32: From Grace Presbytery

Whereas, the Lord and Head of the Church has commanded us to go forth into all the world to preach the
Gospel, teaching and baptizing all who in faith repent and submit to Jesus, and

Whereas, in the history of the Christian Church there has been considerable debate as to who constitutes
the proper recipients of baptism, and even now division exists with our body causing confusion, and

Whereas, our fathers have ably demonstrated the Biblical foundation for infant and believer's baptism.
and

Whereas, division exists as to whether or not true Christian baptism should be administered to those who
upon receiving saving faith present themselves to the church for membership, but who were earlier, either
1) the recipients of a so-called baptism, by a religious body, which claimed the sacraments as
part of a process of justification (as in the case of Roman Catholic, Church of Christ, or
Lutheran Churches),
2) presented by unbelieving parents for so-called infant baptism,
3) baptized as adults or older children (it is understood that these persons were baptized as
unbelievers).
4) presented by parents for "Christening".

Therefore be it resolved, for the unity and obedience of the Church, that Grace Presbytery overture the
Eighth General Assembly, meeting in Savannah, Georgia, to instruct the Permanent Theological Committee to
appoint an ad interim committee to define from God’s Word the proper recipients of Christian Baptism.
Adopted at the Spring Stated Meeting of Grace Presbytery, May 9, 1980.
Attest:
Rev. Norman A. Bagby, Jr
Stated Clerk of Grace Presbytery
Referred back to Grace Presbytery. § 8-69, III, 1; p. 97.

To the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations

##### Overture 6: From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America has had a committee meeting with representatives of the
Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, the Orthodox Presbyterian Church and the Reformed
Presbyterian Church of North America, to talk about “ areas of agreement, difference and difficulties" in
relation to organic union; and

Whereas, contacts with these other denominations have been warm, friendly and suggestive of a mutual
interest for even closer relationships;

Now Therefore Be It Resolved, that Warrior Presbytery does overture the General Assembly to
extend to the Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, the Orthodox Presbyterian Church and the
Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America, a most cordial and fraternal invitation to unite with this
Church in the spirit of the invitation of Numbers 10:29: "W e are journeying unto the place of which the Lord
said, ‘I will give it you': Come thou with us and we will do thee good: for the Lord hath spoken good concerning
Israel!"

TE fredrick S. Carr

15 January 1980

##### Overture 18: From Pacific Presbytery

Whereas, the Orthodox Presbyterian Church is a sister of the Presbyterian Church in America, holding
the same doctrinal standards and practicing the same polity, and

Whereas, there is a need today fora united presbyterian voice for the historic christian faith, a viable
alternative to theologically liberal Presbyterianism on the North American continent, and

Whereas, the Pacific Presbytery is one of three PCA presbyteries most affected by our Lord's mandate to
build His church within the same geographical boundaries as those within which the OPC is at work,
sometimes to the confusion of the world and even other parts of Christ's body.

Therefore, the Pacific Presbytery overtures the Eighth General Assembly to humbly extend an invitation
to the Orthodox Presbyterian Church to join the Presbyterian Church in America, thereby creating one church,
one united witness in the nation and to the world and one fellowship as true brethren in Christ.
Furthermore, should the Eighth General Assembly act upon the above overture in the affirmative, that the
Pacific Presbytery be authorized to immediately discuss with the Northern California, Southern California and
Northwest Presbyteries of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church our mutual concerns and possible redrawing of
boundaries should our presbyteries be joined.
Adopted by Pacific Presbytery January 26. 1980.
Attest:
William F. Woodhall
Stated Clerk
Answered by letter of invitation. See § 8-43, IV, 5; p. 80ff.

##### Overture 28: From the Presbytery of the Ascension

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America did, when she was first called into being as a separate
Church in December, 1973, address a letter to all churches in which she affirmed, "As this new member of the
family of churches of the Lord jesus Christ comes into being, we necessarily profess the Biblical doctrine of the
unity of all who are in Christ. . . We greet all believers in an affirmation of the bond of Christian brotherhood.
We invite into ecclesiastical fellowship all who maintain our principles of faith and order” ; and

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America is committed to the inerrancy of the Bible in the original
autographs and thus to its infallible authority over us in all matters of faith and life; and

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America is committed to the Reformed Faith as set forth in the
westminster confession and catechisms and to presbyterian government asset forth in the Book of Church Order; and

Whereas, as a young Church which is yet in forming, the Presbyterian Church in America would benefit
from the wisdom and experience of others who hold a like faith and polity and who have preceded us in similar
church developments; and

Whereas, in the Presbytery of the Ascension and many other presbyteries there is duplication of efforts
and resources by those who share a common faith as a basis of unity along with many expressions of desire for
such unity; and

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America recognizes that the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, the
Reformed Presbyterian Church, Evangelical Synod, and the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America
all hold the same faith as the Presbyterian Church in America;

Therefore, the Presbytery of the Ascension respectfully overtures the Eighth General Assembly of the
Presbyterian Church in America to invite the Orthodox Presbyterian Church, the Reformed Presbyterian
Church, Evangelical Synod, and the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America to join the Presbyterian Church in America under the terms of her Constitution.
Adopted the twenty-sixth day of February, 1980, at Greensburg, Pa.
Frank D. Moser. Stated Clerk
Answered by letter of invitation. See § 8-43, IV, 5; p. 80ff.

To the Committee of Commissioners on Judicial Business

##### Overture 1: From Grace Presbytery

(Clerk’s note: This overture was received too late for consideration by the Seventh General Assembly, and is
thus carried over to this Assembly .)

Whereas, troubles and difficulties may arise which make it impossible or undesirable that a minister
continue to serve his congregation, even though these troubles and difficulties are not of such a nature that
demand the institution of judicial process against the minister; and

Whereas, the minister may feel compelled to tender the resignation of his pastoral charge, or the church
shall desire to be relieved of its pastor, resulting in the dissolution of the pastoral relation;

Therefore, Grace Presbytery overtures the Seventh General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to institute procedures to amend the Book of Church Order by the addition of anew paragraph 24-2:
When a minister may feel compelled to tender the resignation of his pastoral charge or the church shall desire to
be relieved of its pastor because of an unresolvable situation existing between him and his church, and the
minister is not eligible for retirement nor worthy of discipline, the church shall provide for the support of the
minister subsequent to the dissolution of the pastoral relation in such away and for such a time ai shall receive

<a id="ga08-p39"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=39 printed_page=null -->

the approval of the Presbytery, for a period of not less than 90 days, unless he shall receive a Call to another
work prior to the expiration of this period.
Attest:
Rev. Norman A. Bagby, Jr.
Stated Clerk
May II, 1979
Answered in the negative. § 8-88, III, 11; p. 118.

##### Overture 3: From the Presbytery of Southern Florida

Whereas, it appears that the First General Assembly, when formulating the current wording of
paragraphs 25-6 through 25-9 of the Book of Church Order, intended to allow, though not to recommend,
limited (rotational) terms of active service for Ruling Elders and Deacons (see Recommendation No. 2, Report
of Permanent Sub-Committee on Judicial Business to the Sixth General Assembly, page 188, Minutes of the
Sixth General Assembly), and

Whereas, many individuals within our denomination, in particular churches both using and not using
limited terms, doubt or question whether the current wording of the Book of Church Order does in fact allow
limited terms of active service for Ruling Elders and Deacons as it appears was intended by the First General Assembly, and

Whereas, many of our particular churches are using limited terms of active service for their Ruling
Elders and/or Deacons, and strongly desire to continue to do so, and

Whereas, the particular churches using limited terms of active service also desire that there be no doubt
or questioning as to whether the procedure they a reusing is allowed by the Book of Church Order, and

Whereas, the widespread use within our denomination of a procedure, the allowableness of which under
the Book of Church Order is extensively doubted and questioned, erodes the authority of and respect for the
Book of Church Order and is inimical to effective church government.

Therefore, the Presbytery of Southern Florida hereby overtures the Eighth (1980) General Assembly to
initiate action under the provisions of paragraph 27-2 of the Book of Church Order to amend and thereby clarify
the Book of Church Order by adding the following new paragraph:
"25-10. Instead of electing Ruling Elders and Deacons for indefinite or unlimited terms of active service,
a particular church, by a majority vote a ta congregational meeting, may adopt a system providing for the
election of Ruling Elders or Deacons, or both, for limited terms of active service. In such cases, the terms
of active service shall be at least three years, except to initiate the system or to fill unexpired terms; and
the Session and the Board of Deacons each shall consist of at least three classes elected at regular
intervals. When a congregation limits terms of active service, it shall designate the period, if any, during
which officers shall be ineligible for re-election to active service.”
"A Ruling Elder whose term of active service in a particular church has expired, if otherwise eligible,
may represent that church in the higher courts.
Adopted at the Stated Meeting of Southern Florida Presbytery, October 16, 1979
Attest:
Earl S. Mizell
Stated Clerk
Answered in the negative. § 8-88, III, 12; p. 118.

##### Overture 4: From the Presbytery of the Western Carolinas

Whereas, each year there are elected alternate members of the Permanent Committees of the General Assembly, one Teaching and one Ruling Elder, and

Whereas, these alternate members have an annual cost of a full and regular member, and

Whereas, by the present rule of BOCO 15-1-11 these alternate members are voting members only in the
event of a lack of full committee quorum, and

Whereas, no specific ruling determines whether this shall be a quorum among the Ruling Elders on the
committee, or among the Teaching Elders, or the quorum of the committee as a whole, and

Whereas, by their regular attendance these duly-elected members acquire expertise in the committee's
field of business, and should be able to vote wisely.

Therefore, The Presbytery of the Western Carolinas overtures the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to change section 15-1-11 to replace the last sentence of that paragraph to read: "Each
alternate should attend each meeting and fill any vacancy necessary to take the place of any absentee in the
particular elder-category to which the alternate belongs, and vote only if this substitution is being made.' 1 In
this manner, it will not be necessary for an absence of 3-5 regular committee members for an alternate to
become useful to the General Assembly who elected him, but he may begin to vote whenever just one regular
member in his elder-category is absent. if a teaching elder is absent, the Teaching Elder alternate takes his
place; if a ruling elder is absent, the Ruling Elder alternate makes the substitution.
Adopted by 25th Stated Meeting of the Presbytery of the Western Carolinas, Marin, North Carolina,
November 17, 1979.
A. Boyce Spooner
Stated Clerk
Answered by reference to answer to Overture 29. § 8-88, III, 14; p. 118.

<a id="ga08-p40"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=40 printed_page=null -->

##### Overture 8: From the Presbytery of the Western Carolinas

Whereas, the Book of Church Order (BOCO), paragraph 26-11, provides explicitly for the withdrawal
of congregations from the PCA ‘‘at any time for reasons which seem to it sufficient,'' and

Whereas, the BOCO does not set forth procedures for a congregation to take this important step, and

Whereas, such a significant action should only betaken by a congregation after a proper study of the
matter, and in an orderly way.

Therefore, the Presbytery of the Western Carolinas overtures the General Assembly to direct the
Permanent Committee on Judicial Business to frame a possible amendment to Paragraph 26-11 of the BOCO to
provide for an orderly procedure to handle this matter.
Adopted at the Winter Stated meeting of the Western Carolinas Presbytery, January 15, 1980.
A. Boyce Spooner
Stated Clerk
Answered in the affirmative, and referred to Sub-Committee on Judicial Business.
§8-88,111, 15; p. 118.

##### Overture 14: From the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida

(Note: This overture was presented to Gulf Coast Presbytery, but was not adopted by Presbytery.)

Whereas, the Book of Church Order 15:5 now allows for forty (40) men from seven (7) Presbyteries to
constitute a quorum for General Assembly;

Whereas, this could allow a General Assembly to be called by a special interest minority;

Whereas, the Book of Church Order 26:3 requires a minimum of 1/6th of the total congregation for a
congregational meeting;

Therefore, the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida, proposes that
the Book of Church Order and the Operating Rules for General Assembly be amended as follows:
1. That the number of Presbyteries required to call a General Assembly be at least 1/4th of the total
number of Presbyteries;
2. That the number of Commissioners required to call a General Assembly be the same as the required
number fora congregational meeting in the Book of Church Order 26:3, at least 1/6th of the total
number of Commissioners.
3. That the total number of Teaching and Ruling Elders who are eligible to attend should be the whole
number upon which the 1/6th fraction is based.
4. That if or when the fraction of Commissioners on the floor of General Assembly drops below the
number required for a called Assembly, that the General Assembly suspend business until a true
quorum can be obtained, not just a percentage of those enrolled. If this true quorum cannot be
obtained, General Assembly should be declared adjourned by the Moderator.
Adopted by the Session of Westminster Presbyterian Church, Fort Walton Beach, Florida on November
11,1979.
Attested:
M.C. Hull
Clerk of Session
C. Don Darling
Moderator of Session
Answered in the negative. § 8-88, III, 16; p. 118.

##### Overture 15: From the Presbytery of the Mid-Atlantic

Whereas, a problem exists in calling a pastor to congregations developed through the leadership of an
Organizing Pastor; and

Whereas, it is not that these congregations want someone else as pastor but need a constitutional way to
call the Organizing Pastor the same day that they are organized; and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order provides away fora mission group to nominate ruling elders before
they are organized, the same principle could be applied to the selection of a pastor; and

Whereas, the proposed amendment could allow the Presbytery to authorize the Commission elected to
organize the church to approve the Call and install the pastor if the man is already a member of the same
Presbytery;

Therefore, be it resolved that the Book of Church Order be amended by adding the following to chapter
5—
“ 5 — 4 the following procedures maybe used in the selection of a pastor ina newly organized
congregation:
“ (1) Not less than thirty days prior to the date of organization the petitioners shall elect from their own
body a Pulpit Nominating Committee. This election shall take place at a meeting of the petitioners
announced at least one week in advance. Only those who have made a written commitment to
membership in the new church are eligible to vote at this meeting.
“ (2) The Pulpit Committee may report at the organizational meeting of the congregation, or any
subsequent congregational meeting called for that purpose.
‘ ‘(3) if at the organizational meeting a pastor is called who is a member of the organizing Presbytery, he
may be installed at that time by the Presbytery or a Commission authorized by the Presbytery to do
so. If the Pastor elect is not a member of the organizing Presbytery, his Call must be prosecuted

<a id="ga08-p41"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=41 printed_page=null -->

under the provisions of Chapter 21 of the Book of Church Order.''
Adopted at the Winter Stated Meeting of the Mid-Atlantic Presbytery, 22 January 1980.
Attest:
Leon F. Wardell
Stated Clerk
Answered in the negative. § 8-88, III, 18; p. 118.

##### Overture 16: From the Presbytery of the Mid-Atlantic

Whereas, in those Presbyteries where there are a large number of ministers, a better balance between
ruling and teaching elders is needed; and

Whereas, a review of the statistics for the end of 1978 shows that one-half of the Presbyteries of the
Presbyterian Church in America have a disproportionate ratio of teaching elders to ruling elders; and

Whereas, in those areas where the church has officers, educational institutions, or even an aggressive
church planting ministry, the ratio of ministers to organized churches becomes disproportionate;

Therefore, be it resolved that the Book of Church Order be amended by the addition to chapter 14-1 as
follows —
“ Amend paragraph 14-1 by adding "When a Presbytery has 50% more Teaching Elders on its roll than
the number of churches on its roll, each church may be represented by two Ruling Elders for the first 350
communing members or fraction thereof."

##### Overture 22: From the Presbytery of Southern Florida

Whereas, the BCO 25-1 calls for the congregations to responsibly submit names to the Church Sessions of
those who are "active male members who qualify . . . etc" and

Whereas, the BCO no where defines what it means by "active" and

Whereas, every male member of congregations of the Presbyterian Church in America, while assumed to
be active because there exists no "inactive list" and yet every church session knows some men to be so
infrequent in the worship and work of the church as to disqualify them from the sacred offices and

Whereas, regular faithful attendance is both a command of the lord of the church and necessary fora
good example to the church, and

Whereas, different congregations offer varying degrees of activity within the various church programs,

Now Therefore Be It Resolved, by the Presbytery of Southern Florida:
' 'That the Presbytery of Southern Florida believes it to be the responsibility of the local Church Sessions
to determine whether names submitted to it of prospective church officers are indeed "active male
members who meet the qualifications of the Word. " And that local sessions should consistently apply
their interpretation of what it means to be "active" from year to year or so inform the congregations of
any changes. Furthermore that men should not be nominated with the hopes that the high offices of Elder
or Deacons will make them more faithful or interested in the Church but because they have shown
unfailing interest in the worship and work by their past diligence. " (See minutes of G.A. 1979 Page 80:3)
Attest
Earl Mizell
Stated Clerk
Amended and answered in the affirmative. § 8-88, III, 20; p. 119.

##### Overture 23: From the Presbytery of Southern Florida

Whereas, the Presbyterian Church in America holds to the form of Presbyterian government in which
Church Sessions, Presbyteries and the General Assembly are courts of the Church with defined powers.

And whereas, it has come to our attention that the Judicial Committee of the General Assembly has
attempted to give advice and interpretation to individuals or congregations prior to seeking the advice of the
Presbyteries which would have original jurisdiction, and

Whereas, the General Assembly has at times not agreed with the interpretation or advice of the Judicial
Committee making the committee’s efforts futile and their advice incorrect as expressing the mind of the
Assembly,

Now Therefore Be It Resolved, that the Presbytery of Southern Florida request the General Assembly to
instruct the Judicial Committee to handle only those cases which come properly by way of appeal after first
coming before the courts of original jurisdiction, namely the Church Sessions, and the Presbyteries, and that
churches or individuals with grievances should first proceed through proper channals of the Presbyterian
Church system before going to the committees of the General Assembly!
Attest
Earl Mizell
Stated Clerk
Answered in the negative. § 8-88, III, 21; p. 119.

congregations.
Believing, that all Scripture is self-attesting and being Truth, requires the human mind whole-heartedly
to subject itself in all its activities to the authority of Scripture complete as the Word of God. standing written in
the sixty-six books of the Holy Bible, all therein being verbally inspired by Almighty God, and therefore
without error; and

and the Larger and ShorterCatechisms set forth the system of doctrine taught in Scripture, and recognizing that

and proclaimed for the edification and government of Christian people, for the propagation of the faith and for

--------------------------Presbytery for organization as required in Chapter 5 of the Book of Church Order.

Mexico, Hawaii, Oregon, and Washington;

with the organization of three churches in California and the reception of a large congregation in Washington;

with the developing of two new works. And

Whereas, the cost of travel is still a major problem with the great distances involved. Not merely to get to
Presbytery meetings to have a quorum, but for committees to function properly; and the assistance provided by

##### Overture 20: From Presbytery of Central Florida

Whereas, the Fifth General Assembly in the matter of the erection of the Presbytery of Central Florida
did adopt boundaries which are ambiguous and incomplete, to wit:
( 1) Southern boundary is defined as the southern borders of Sarasota and Manatee counties. Manatee
County lies north of Sarasota County, therefore boundary should be the southern boundary of one or
the other of these counties, not both.
(2) Southern boundary as defined omits the eastern border of Sarasota County, the southern portion of
the eastern border of Manatee County, the eastern border of Hardee County, the eastern portion of
the southern border of Polk County, and the southern portion of the eastern border of Osceola
County.

Whereas, the Mission To The United States Committee of the General Assembly has published a map
which defines properly the southern boundary.

Therefore, the Presbytery of Central Florida does overture the 8th General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to correct the southern boundary description of the Presbytery of Central Florida to read as
follows:
Southern boundary be the southern and eastern borders of Sarasota County, the southern portion of the
eastern border of Manatee County, the southern and eastern borders of Hardee County, the eastern
portion of the southern border of Polk County, the southern border and the southern portion of the eastern
border of Osceola County and the southern border of Brevard County.
Adopted at the Winter meeting of Presbytery. January 15, 1980.
Attest:
Charles W. Ambler. Jr.
Stated Clerk
Answered in the affirmative. § 8-50, III, 7; p. 86.

##### Overture 26: From the Session of Covenant Church

Whereas, the boundaries of the New River Presbytery are very broad and the nine churches distantly
scattered; thereby, making fellowship and cooperation difficult, and

Whereas, the /97# yearbook of the Presbyterian Church in America records avery poor financial report
of total contributions to the Presbytery by its churches of $6.164 of which approximately 80% of that amount
goes to one mission work in Princeton; thereby, making it financially impossible to begin other new works or
support other causes, and

Whereas, two of the nine churches have only reported 17 and 34 members respectively and have not had
any reported additions in 1978. one has not had a pastor in several years and the other is ina two field situation,
and

Whereas, three of the churches (Lebanon. Little River, and Westminsterl and the mission, (Princeton (are
closer to the bounds of other Presbylerys, and

Whereas, several Presbytery meetings in the past have shown very serious divisions, doctrinal disagree
ment, and a disregard for the Book of Church Order and the Westminster Confession of Faith, and

Whereas, it is apparent to this session that the New River Presbytery does nothing but meet four times a
year, supports a struggling mission work with most of its money, and shows no viability or effectiveness in
starting new churches, nor is financially able to start any churches, and

Whereas, the New River Presbytery has been cited by the General Assembly for improper action, and

Whereas, the New River Presbytery has shown its inability to deal with one of its churches and has seen a
division take place, which has possibly reduced the number of churches in the Presbytery and has definitely
affected the financial base of the Presbytery, and.

Whereas, the Presbytery failed to deal with one of its ministers, who had written slanderous remarks
about another minister in the New River Presbytery;

financial weaknesses, the number of churches, geographical locations, serious divisions and doctrinal
differences, the session of the Covenant Presbyterian Church, believing that the New River Presbytery is not
viable as a Reformed Presbyterian witness in the Presbyterian Church in America hereby overtures the New
River Presbytery to overture the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to dissolve the New
River Presbytery and approve the following plan:

Whereas, The General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America has made an effort to increase
the participation of Ruling Elders in the functions of the Assembly, and

Whereas, some Ruling Elders are discouraged over the imbalance between Ruling and Teaching Elders
representatives to the Presbytery and the General Assembly,

Be It Therefore Resolved, that the Seventh General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America
ask the Permanent Committee on Judicial Business to study this imbalance and make recommendations to

<a id="ga08-p45"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=45 printed_page=null -->

General Assembly as to a solution which would be in line with the Presbyterian Church in America's Doctrine
of the Parity of Elders.

Earl S. Mizell
Stated Clerk
Referred to the Permanent Committee on Administration § 8-103, 111, 8; p. 122.
Overture 5 to the Seventh General Assembly: From Evangel Presbytery

Whereas, the time of the General Assembly for adequate consideration of all matters is limited, and

Whereas, printed reports are required of the Committees of Commissioners and ad interim committees
when reporting to the General Assembly, and

Whereas, there is a requirement under Sub-sections 8-11 (4) and 10-2 of the Rules of Assembly Operations that the full text of each report be read by the Chairman before comment or action, and

Whereas, the reading of such reports is time consuming and nonproductive when the Commissioners
hold such reports in their hands.

Therefore, Evangel Presbytery overtures the Seventh General Assembly to amend the Rules for the
General Assembly Operations as follows:
( 1) Following the first sentence of Sub-section 8 -11 (4) add the following sentence:
"The assembly may waive the reading of any particular report by a majority vote of the Commissioners
present and voting. "
(2) Following the second sentence of Sub-section 10-2, add the following sentence:
' The Assembly may waive the reading of any particular report by a majority vote of the Commissioners
present and voting''
Adopted at the Stated Meeting of Evangel Presbytery, October 2 1, 1978.
Answered in the affirmative. §8-103,111, 18; p. 123.

( I) Organization of General Assembly Meeting.
1-3 That the following be added. "The second order of business shall be the election of a
Moderator-in-Nomination for the next succeeding General Assembly. This Moderator-in-

nomination by the Stated Clerk at the next succeeding General Assembly provided he is a duly

Overture 7 to the Seventh General Assembly: From the Presbytery of the Evangel

Whereas, during the first several days of the General Assembly, the pressure of time to complete the
business of the General Assembly is not so evident, and
Wereas, much important business considered on the final two days of the General Assembly may
receive inadequate debate and consideration by the General Assembly, and

Whereas, we are desirous of expediting all business of the General Assembly with adequate debate for
all major issues.

Therefore, Evangel Presbytery overtures the Seventh General Assembly to amend the Rules for
Assembly Operations as follows:
Section IV The Assembly Arrangements
Add subsection 4-3 to read as follows:
"4-3 after adoption of a docket of the business to be considered fora day the assembly shall not
adjourn for the day until all business on the docket has been considered and dealt with. This rule
shall not preclude the assembly from suspending further action on a particular matter until a
subsequent time of the Assembly when additional information, unavailable at the time, must be
obtained for proper consideration of the matter.
Adopted at the Stated Meeting of Evangel Presbytery. October 21. 1978.
Attested by:
Hubert C. Stewart

Overture 16 to the Seventh General Assembly: From the Presbytery of North Georgia

Whereas, an ecclesiastical body which adopts positions on substantive doctrinal and moral issues by a
bare majority vote runs the grave risks of reducing the credibility and authority of its actions, alienating the
church and promoting division within it, wasting time, and moving to conclusions (perhaps wrong ones) before
the Holy Spirit has brought His people to one mind on the issue in question.

Therefore, Be It Resolved, that North Georgia Presbytery request the General Assembly to take the
following action:
"Resolutions which would state Assembly position on substantive moral or doctrinal issues shall require
a two-thirds vote of registered commissioners in order to pass.''
Adopted unanimously at the Stated Winter Meeting of North Georgia Presbytery. January 20. 1979.

R. G. Valentine

Overture 28 to the Seventh General Assembly: From Grace Presbytery

Whereas, the Rules for Assembly Operations are intended solely to guide the conduct of business during
a meeting of the General Assembly; and

Whereas, the Rules for Assembly Operations are not intended to direct the duties of the officers of the
General Assembly, except as they apply to the conduct of the business of a meeting of the General Assembly;
and

Whereas, any such rule ought to be a part of the Bylaws of the Presbyterian Church in America;

Therefore, Grace Presbytery overtures the Seventh General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to amend the Rules for Assembly Operations by striking paragraph e-7, and the Bylaws of the
Presbyterian Church in America (A Corporation) by adding to Article III (Officers), Section 3, a sentence:
The Clerk shall be an advisory member of the Sub-Committee on Inter-Church Relations, and an
advisory member of any such other committee as the General Assembly may direct.
Date: May I 1, 1979

Rev. Norman A. Bagby. Jr.

Whereas, the election of an assistant parliamentarian at the Sixth General Assembly proved successful;

Therefore, Grace Presbytery overtures the Seventh General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America to amend the Rules for Assembly Operations by striking paragraph 3-8 and by inserting new
paragraph 1-6, which shall read:
The Moderator shall, after consultation with the Stated Clerk, appoint a parliamentarian to serve for the

7-70 Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Administration to the Seventh
General Assembly
The following recommendations were ruled out of order since the recommended changes
required a two-thirds vote of all registered commissioners, and there were an insufficient
number of commissioners to enact them. They were thus carried over to the next
Assembly.
(Clerk's Note: The recommendations of this report have been renumbered so that those
items might be grouped together.)
25. That the Assembly amend the “ Rules for Assembly Operations” as follows:
Add new paragraphs 6-2 and 6-3:
6-2 Any report requesting amendments to the Constitution of the PCA or
interpretation thereof by the General Assembly shall be referred to the
Permanent Committee on Judicial Business for its recommendation.
6-3 The report of the Assembly’s Nominating Committee may be amended by
nominations from the floor, which shall be received in the following way:
1. Such nominations shall be made in writing on forms provided by the
Office of the Stated Clerk, and shall be submitted to the Stated
Clerk.
2. Nominations shall indicate the consent of the nominees to serve, if
elected.
26. That Overture 5 (p. 27) from Evangel Presbytery be answered in the affirma
tive. Note the obvious error (Sub-section 8-11 and Sub-section 10-2).
Reason: To expedite Assembly Operations.
27. That Overture 6 from Evangel Presbytery (p.28) be answered in the
affirmative.
28. That Overture 7 from Evangel Presbytery (p.28) be answered in the negative.
Reason: that this was not a workable solution to a genuine problem.
29. That Overture 28 from Grace Presbytery (p.31) be answered in the affirmative.
Reason: This corrects the fact that the Stated Clerk was not to be an ex-officio
member of said committees.
30. That Overture 29 from Grace Presbytery (p.31) be answered in the negative.
Reason: The present procedure of appointing an assistant parliamentarian is
satisfactory.
31. That Overture 2 (p.27) referred from Judicial Business be referred to the
Permanent Committee on Administration.
32. That Overture 31 from Grace Presbytery (p.32) be answered in the negative.
Reason: The present procedure followed this year satisfactorily deals with the
problem.

6-107
From the Constitutional Documents Committee Report to the Sixth General Assembly
The Constitutional Documents Committee has done two areas of work during the past year. The first
regards the study edition of the Confession of Faith and Catechisms with Scriptural footnotes.
In compliance with the Fifth General Assembly we have prepared a study edition of the doctrinal
standards using the edition of the Free Presbyterian Church of Scotland with the three changes in our edition
being substituted with the Scriptural proof texts of the Orthodox Presbyterian Church edition.
The Christian Education and Publications Comittee has prepared the paste on corrections and now have
the study guide available for $2.00.
The Committee has also worked with the special Editorial Sub-Committee in the assignment of preparing
a complete and edited addition of the Book of Church Order in the near future. A partial report of the progress is
contained in this report.
slow progress is being made with the scriptural proof text for the Book of Church Order and it is apparent
that such an assignment cannot be completed until the editorialized copy is in hand. This is in accord with the
Minutes of the 1977 General Assembly, page 189.
Recommendations:
(1) That members take advantage of the Westminster Confession of Faith and Catechisms with Scriptural
proof texts, study edition and make suggestions to the Constitutional Documents Committee regarding
additions or deletions
Referred to the Committee for Christian Education and Publications. § 7-41, III, 23; p.
105. See §8-29, III, 9; p. 73.
To the Committee of Commissioners on Judicial Business
3-70 Report of Constitutional Documents Committee Continued (3-69)
A temporary statement was adopted to be placed at the beginning of the Directory
of Worship until a more precise statement can be prepared by the Constitutional
Documents Committee. The Constitutional Documents Committee was directed to
prepare a statement on the relative authority of the Constitutional documents, which is to
be returned to the next Assembly. Constitutional Documents Committee dismissed, §

To the Committee of Commissioners on Stewardship
Overture 26 to the Seventh General Assembly: From Warrior Presbytery

Whereas, it is past time to begin responsible stewardship in the PCA, and

Whereas, we must have faith in God's provision, and yet we also must not tempt God, and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order, 15-1. principle 3, states, ‘The work of the Church as set forth in
the Great Commission is one work, being implemented at the General Assembly level through equally essential
committees," and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order, 15-1, principle 4 states, “ It is the responsibility of every member
and every member congregation to support the whole work of the denomination as they be led in their
conscience held captive to the Word of God, ' and

Whereas, the Book of Church Order, 15-1, principle 5 states, "It is the responsibilty of the General Assembly to evaluate needs and resources and to act on priorities for the most effective fulfillment of the Great
Commission” and yet, since the majority of money is designated, the General Assembly cannot act upon its
priorities but upon those established by the giving patterns, and

Whereas, a unified budget is in keeping with viewing the work of the Church as one work; and
supporting the whole work of the denomination and is apparently essential if the General Assembly is to act
upon its own priorities, and

Whereas, a unified budget with appropriate limitations presents no real problems ina denomination
where the inerrant and infallible Word of God is upheld, and

Whereas, the various committees are sending many men around to the various Churches, with a large
majority of these men being itinerated under the Committee on Mission to the World, and

Whereas, the seeking of funds for designated purposes in this manner amounts to an unbalanced appeal
which naturally results in unbalanced giving, and

Whereas, the itinerating of missionary candidates has many worthwhile features, and

Whereas, nevertheless, the itinerating of missionary candidates to raise theirown support is demeaning,
and

<a id="ga08-p49"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=49 printed_page=null -->

Whereas, a person's support-raising ability is not necessarily proportional to his ability for a specific
missionary calling, and

Whereas, itineration of these men in support of the whole work of the Church through undesignated
giving would certainly advance the whole work of the Church in general and each committee in particular;

Therefore, Warrior Presbytery overtures the General Assembly to adopt the following provisions for
promoting the whole work of the denomination:
1. That the Committee on Administration shall submit a budget each year based on (a) a reasonable
projected income and (b) a responsible and strategic balance of the budget between the committees,
and
2. That all undesignated funds shall be divided among the committees proportionate to their respective
shares of the budget, and
3. That the three permanent program committees of the General Assembly and all those sent out under
or by them shall seek only undesignated financial support and with the PCA Messenger and the
Sub-Committee on Stewardship they shall positively promote undesignated giving for the whole
work of the denomination, except for those works allowed support only through designated giving,
and
4. That contributors sending designated support for works other than those allowed support only
through designated giving be written and encouraged to send undesignatedsupport, and
5. That the budget shall not restrict the maximum spending of any committee if itsreceipts should
exceed the budgeted amount, but that any expenditures in excess of the budget must be for General Assembly mandated, high priority program items and not special causes, and
6. That any designated money still received shall be used as designated without in any way affecting
the percentage distribution of undesignated funds, and
7. That all who work under the three permanent program committees shall be supported out of the
General Fund of each respective committee except that single "sending bodies" in the sense used in
the MTW Manual may give partial or full support which would be designated.
Adopted by Presbytery at its Stated Meeting. April 17, 1979.
Attest:
Fred Carr
Stated Clerk
Answered in the negative. § 8-80, III, 11; p. 109.
D. JUDICIAL CASES — APPEALS
Case 1: An Appeal of Victor E. Lockman Appealing the Action of the Gulf Coast Presbytery of the PCA
on Oct. 13,1979.

### I. BASIS OF THE APPEAL

It is apparent from the language of Mcllwain Memorial Presbyterian Church's (hereafter referred to as
Mcllwain) letter notifying me that my membership had been terminated (letter Jan. 29, 1979) that judicial
action had in fact been taken, for repentance on my part was stated to be a requirement of renewing my
affiliation with Mcllwain.
Mcllwain must have held a closed trial of sorts, with the appellant absent, on Jan. 27, 1979 in order to
render the above noted judgment. My Jan. 18, 1979 letter of resignation, withdrawn on Jan. 24, 1979, lists
some of the unjust irregularities perpetrated by Mcllwain in their proceedings against Appellant.
Gulf Coast Presbytery appears to have recognized the document filed against Mcllwain as an appeal
because;
(1.) It was on the docket as such for Oct 13,1979.
(2.) Presbytery's Fact Finding Committee advised that HOC. 28-5, line 5 requires a church to act through
her court and if so, it is appealable. The committee also recommended that the Appellant be given a
"REGULAR TRIAL", thereby implying that an IRREGULAR trial had taken place.
(3.) Presbytery found the document to be in order as an appeal (BOC 43-7 (I)), though they
"officially" voted down hearing the parties (BOC 43-7 (2)). Unofficially Mr. Donald A. Dunker-
ley presented a five minute accusatory talk against the Appellant, to which Appellant had five
minutes to reply
(4.) Presbytery further acknowledged that an appeal had been lodged when they, by a vote of 11 to 10,
refused to reconsider it as a complaint.
Therefore, from the history of Appellant's case, it appears that trial-like judicial actions have taken place
at both the Session and Presbytery levels, and that hence. Appellant is justified in carrying the matter to the
General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America. Else it would be possible for a party to be removed
from office and membership roll of a church, and all this against one's will, by administrative procedures and
that without recourse. Such a course of action would be contrary to both the Word of God (Mat. 18:15-17, etc.)
and the Book of Church Order 28-5 and chapters 32 through 34, as well as being contrary to sound reason
II. SERIOUS IRREGULARITIES IN THE PROCEEDINGS OF THE GULF COAST
PRESBYTERY’S MEETING OF OCTOBER 13, 1979 HELD AT WARRINGTON
CHURCH, PENSACOLA, FLORIDA
1. Mr. Donald A Dunkerley deliberated and voted on the instant case when it was appealed to

<a id="ga08-p50"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=50 printed_page=null -->

Presbytery, contrary to the BOC and scriptural standards of justice.

A. BOC 36-11 disqualifies a member of a court who has given testimony in a case from sitting as a judge if either party makes objection. Mr. Dunkerley in effect, by his accusatory statements about Appellant was giving testimony against him. Appellant objected to his voting.

B. BOC 33-19 excludes from sitting in judgment on a case one who has acted as counsel for the accused. Mr. Dunkerley so acted when he repeatedly defended and spoke on behalf of the session on the floor of Presbytery.

C. BOC 40-2 states that “When the proceedings of a lower court are brought before a higher court, the members of the lower court shall not lose the right to sit, deliberate and vote in the higher court, except in cases of appeal or complaint.” (Emphasis added) Mr. Dunkerley voted against my appeal (twice) and also against reconsidering it as a complaint.

2. Mr. Dunkerley prosecuted the case before hand by virtue of his many prejudicial statements against the Appellant as a person from the floor before the Presbytery voted. He charged the Appellant with the following offenses;

A. Accusing the innocent
B. Refusing to stand trial
C. Holding heretical views.
D. Renouncing the authority of the session
E. Having a past record of stirring up trouble in churches.

These unfounded charges may well have persuaded the Presbytery adversely in regard to the Appellant’s cause.

3. Mr. Dunkerley intimidated and applied pressure to the Presbytery before they voted by suggesting that a vote against McIlwain might well result in McIlwain withdrawing from the P.C.A.

4. McIlwain failed to abide by BOC 43-5 by NOT sending the record of the case up to Presbytery.

### III. THE BIBLE TEACHES THAT ACCESS TO THE HIGHEST COURT SHOULD ALWAYS BE AVAILABLE

1. Members of God’s Kingdom always have access to God’s Throne, the highest court in the universe, through prayer, and with a Divine advocate.

2. In ancient Israel there was always access to the highest court in the land, first, with Moses in that seat of judgment, and later, when kings reigned and ruled over the highest court in the land.

Yea, the Bible everywhere teaches that God loves Justice and Judgment and that it is wrong to pervert a just cause. Christ particularly denounced the legalistic ways of his opponents who sought by the traditions of men to escape their responsibilities and to nullify the law of God.

IV. Wherefore, Appellant respectfully prays this court to take whatsoever measures it deems appropriate, and, in the interest of truth and justice, to rectify the grievances stated above.

Appellant, VICTOR E. LOCKMAN, swears by God’s most Holy Name that the above statements are true and may be verified.

Signed on this 19th day of October, in the 1979th year of our LORD.

See § 8-13, 1; p. 62.

VICTOR E. LOCKMAN

Mr. Bob Kresge
