Presbyterian Church in America

I, Rod Mays, a teaching elder of the New River Presbytery of the Presbyterian Church in America do hereby issue a complaint to the General Assembly concerning the failure of the New River Presbytery to deal with one of its ministers (Mr. Linwood Wilkes) who was reported to be guilty of writing slanderous letters concerning another minister in New River Presbytery, (Mr. Bill Fitzhenry).

Whereas, these accusations of slander were reported to the Presbytery’s committee on Ministers and Candidates,

Whereas, that committee moved to take action against Mr. Wilkes,

Whereas, before the accusations were brought before Presbytery, a motion was moved, seconded, and approved to drop the discussion of matters relating to the accusations of Mr. Wilkes,

Therefore, I do protest and complain (BCO-44) about this failure of presbytery to deal with reported scandalous activity involving one of its ministers.

See § 8-13, 2; p. 62, and § 8-84; p. 111.

Rod S. Mays

**Case 3: Complaint of Teaching Elders Byron Snapp and James M. Hope against Calvary Presbytery.**

The text of a complaint against the actions of Calvary Presbytery in the matter of accepting a candidate for ordination under the extraordinary clause when there was no reason for using the extraordinary clause. The said candidate had chosen not to take more than one quarter of Hebrew as he did not at that time plan to come into the PCA.

<a id="ga08-p51"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=51 printed_page=null -->

The undersigned hereby file a complaint regarding the following motion that was adopted by Calvary
Presbytery at its stated winter meeting Thursday, Jan. 24, 1980: "That (the candidate) be examined by
Presbytery under the extraordinary clause (Book of Church Order 22 A ) "
Respectfully submitted,
Byron Snapp
James M. Hope
Date, January 28, 1980
REASONS FOR THE COMPLAINT
1) It appears that more than one quarter of Hebrew is required to meet the standards set forth in BCO 22-4
in light of the following: a) All the approved Seminaries of the PCA recognize the need of more than one quarter
of Hebrew to meet the Hebrew requirement set forth in BCO 22-4; b) On page 190 of the Minutes of the 7th
General Assembly of the PCA the 2t2 program has five quarters of Hebrew and Hebrew exegesis recommended
as a necessary part of the curriculum; c) By bringing the candidate in under the extraordinary clause, the
Presbytery, in effect, went on record as stating that his Hebrew preparation was insufficient to meet the
requirements of BCO Tl-A.
2) The candidate took but one quarter of Hebrew. He passed it. He did not take further courses although
further courses were available. In light of this fact, the use of the extraordinary clause appears to us to be
improper.
3) We believe that the extraordinary clause is to be used only in extraordinary cases. We do not believe
this to be an extraordinary case as a) the candidate is a young man;b) he passed his first quarter of Hebrew; c) he
could be a student supply at the church which called him and continue his study of Hebrew at Columbia Bible
College Graduate School, Columbia, S.C. of which he is an alumnus, as he is to be pastor of northeast chapel
in Columbia, S.C. ;d) The reasons which the candidate gave for not taking more Hebrew are as follows: “ To be
honest, i took only one quarter of hebrews imply because i thought i would fail the next quarter. Grades were
give nona curve basis and i was always at the bottom. I might add that the PCA was no part of my vocational
plans at the time, so my main motive in securing a hebrews kill was simply so that i could lookup words and
stumble through commentaries, not taking any certain number of hours.' ’
4) If the extraordinary clause is used in this manner, the precedent is set for the relaxing of any
requirement set forth in BCO 22-4.
5) We desire to have the following question answered: "What is the proper use of the extraordinary
clause?''.
See § 8-13, 3; p. 63, and § 8-36; p. 77.
Case 4: Complaint of Ruling Elder James H. Campbell, et al Against Mid-Atlantic Presbytery
February 6, 1980
The Reverend Morton H. Smith, Stated Clerk.
General Assembly, Presbyterian Church in America
P.O. Box 312
Brevard, North Carolina 28712

Whereas, as the Judicial Commission of the Mid-Atlantic Presbytery, Presbyterian Church in America,
a ta hearing on november 2, 1979, on four charges against Robert C. Schoof, did render an injustice in the
judgment and censure, which action is contrary to the BCO, and possible manifestation of prejudice in the case,
the undersigned hereby complains to the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America of this
action of the Mid-Atlantic Presbytery in the above entitled matter, and for reasons in support of such complaint,
states the following:
Charge 1. The Commission found Mr. Schoof guilty of violating the civil laws of Virginia and Section
60-1 BCO. I do not complain of this finding. The Commission found Mr. Schoof not guilty of violating Sect.
60-2 and 60-6. These later findings are in conflict with the first, as the civil laws of Virginia require that a
lawful minister perform the marriage, as does Sect. 60-2. By not convicting Mr. Schoof of violating 60-2,
Mid-Atlantic Presbytery states that a seminary student is an ecclesiastical official, that is, a lawful minister.
Sect. 60-6 requires ministers to be careful they transgress neither the laws of God, nor the laws of the
community.
Charge 2. The Commission found Mr. Schoof not guilty of signing an official document stating he had
joined his daughter and her husband in marriage, when the official document, bearing Mr. Schoof s signature,
was introduced in evidence.
Charge 3. The Commission found Mr. Schoof not guilty of conducting an illegal Congregational
meeting, when two of four Elders present at Session meeting setting forth the call for the Congregational
meeting testified otherwise.
Charge 4. The Commission found Mr. Schoof not guilty of violating Sect. 57-2 and 57-6 when
testimony introduced showed no ruling Elder present at the Baptism and only a selected group of less than eight
members of the congregation present.
i F.
copy: Leon c u/ a i.
Wardel Sincerely in Christ,
James H. Campbell
Acting Stated Clerk Ruli Elder
Mid-Atlantic Presbytery

Case 5: Complaint of Teaching Elder Carl W. Bogue et al Against the Presbytery of the Ascension
March 3, 1980
The Rev. Morton H. Smith, Stated Clerk
General Assembly, Presbyterian Church in America
P.O. Box 312
Brevard, N.C. 28712

Whereas, in the action of the Presbytery of the Ascension of the Presbyterian Church in America, at the
stated meeting February 26, 1980, in Greensburg, Pennsylvania, respecting the sustaining of the trials for
ordination and the approving of the call to a campus ministry of Mr. Sam Serio, which action is contrary to The
Westminster Confession of Faith and the Book of Church Order, the undersigned hereby complain to The
General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America of this action of the Presbytery of the Ascension.
There are two complaints which here follow, along with the reasons supporting the complaints.
Complaint #1
The trials for ordination of Mr. Sam Serio were sustained by the Presbytery of the Ascension which
action was contrary to a fundamental teaching of the Westminster Confession of Faith.
History: Under examination before the Candidates for Church Vocations Committee and before the
whole Presbytery Mr. Serio affirmed his belief that none of the miraculous gifts had ceased since the Apostolic
age. With specific regard to the miraculous gift of speaking in an “ unknown tongue” Mr. Serio affirmed its
contemporary practice, which when miraculously interpreted by another person, communicated knowledge
from God. Specifically, the origin of such knowledge from God was said to be God the Holy Spirit speaking
through the individual in an unknown tongue. Neither Mr. Serio nor any member of Presbytery indicated that
the candidate’s answers were to be construed as other than specified in this summary paraphrase. Since such
knowledge is here affirmed as being directly given by the Holy Spirit through the miraculous gift of speaking a
language unknown and never studied by the speaker and through the corresponding miraculous gift of
interpretation, the complainants understand such a phenomenon as direct revelation from God. This conclusion
was not disputed, even though the candidate was sustained.
Reasons for the Complaint:
(1) Such a view is in direct conflict with the Scriptural position of our Confession of Faith in 1:1
which declares such revelation to be commited “ wholly unto writing" for the reason that
"those former ways of God's revealing His will unto His people being now ceased."
(2) Such a view is in direct conflict with the Scriptural position of our Confession of Faith
summarized in 1:6 concerning the sufficiency of Scripture, "unto which nothing at any time is
to be added, whether by new revelations of the Spirit or traditions of men. ’’
(3) such a view is indirect conflict with the Book of Church Order, Section 7-1, which says in
part: “ Such officers and gifts related to new revelation have no successors since God
completed His revelation at the conclusion of the Apostolic Age."
(4) Such a view is in direct conflict with the non-constitutional but approved "Pastoral Letter” of
the Second General Assembly (Minutes, pp. 171-175):
“ The General Assembly suggests however, that: 1. Any view of the tongues as
experienced in our time which conceives of it as an experience by which revelation is
received from God is contrary to the finalized character of revelation in Scriptures” (p.
173).
“ Such miracles were signs by which God communicated divine truth or confirmed that
the speaker indeed spoke from God. These miracles related to revelation have ceased,
since revelation was completed with the closing of the Canon in the New Testament
era” (pp. 173-174).
“ ... The General Assembly would recommend:..................................................................
3. Careful training, examination and selection of officers and others in the place of
teaching and leadership in the church to assure a consistency of commitment to
Scripture and the Reformed faith and to the health and unity of the church;
4 . Preaching and teaching of the Doctrine of the Holy Spirit and His work as taught in
Scripture and the Standaids of the church . . . "(pp. 174- 175).
( 5 ) Such an exception to the Confession is open to grave abuse, not the least of which is a
defection from the doctrines of the canon and sola Scriptura.
Complaint # 2
The approval of a call to Mr. sam se riot oa campus ministry was contrary to the Book of Church Order
provisions for such calls.
Reasons for the complaint:
(1) such approval is contrary to the Book of Church Order, Section 21-1, that: “ A proper call
must be written and in the hands of the Presbytery prior to being acted upon by a Presbytery. It
must include . . . assurance that the definite work will afford the liberty to proclaim and
practice fully and freely the whole counsel of God, as contained in the Scriptures and
understood in the Westminster Confession of Faith such written assurance was not in the
call; thus it was not in proper order.
( 2 ) Section 21-1 of the Book of Church Order also states: “ It shall be in accord with the Book of Church Order, Chapter 8. ” In Section 8 of Chapter 8 a teaching elder ins uc ba ministry is

<a id="ga08-p53"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=53 printed_page=null -->

“ to make full proof of his ministry by disseminating the Gospel for the edification of the
Church. ’' Such proof was not and could not be made since our Church is not present in that
area to be edified, nor is the planting of such a Church the goal of this ministry. Rather Mr.
Serio will be under a board made up of leaders of The American Baptist Church, the
Assemblies of God Church, and the Church of God. There is no consistent Reformed witness
of any kind with which Mr. Serio would have any relationship.
(3) Such a call does not conform to the non-constitutional but approved "Manual for Campus
Ministries, Presbyterian Church in America” of the Seventh General Assembly (Minutes, pp.
205-218). Such ministers, even if working with para-church organizations, are to be "under
the guidance and supervision” of PCA Churches or Presbyteries, or the GA MUS Subcommittee on Campus Ministries (pp. 209, 214). “ The ministry is a work of the Presbyterian Church in America” (p. 211), and "the calling and sending body is the commissioning,
ordaining, or installing body, as the case may require” (p. 214). Since the calling body is
utterly non-Presbyterian, it could hardly ordain and install a PCA Teaching Elder.
The undersigned complainants do hereby complain against the action of the Presbytery of the Ascension
and ask that the General Assembly review this matter and declare the action of the February 26, 1980, meeting
of the Presbytery of the Ascension in sustaining the trials for ordination and approving the call of Mr. Sam Serio
to be null and void.
For the cause of Christ and His Kingdom,
Carl W. Bogue, Teaching Elder
Gary Spencer, Ruling Elder
David G. McKay, Teaching Elder
Peter Stazen, II, Ruling Elder
See § 8-13, 5; p. 63; § 8-63, p. 92. Alvin W. Smith, Teaching Elder
F. JUDICIAL CASES — REFERENCES
Reference 1: From Gulf Coast Presbytery of a case regarding Victor Lockman, the Mcllwain Session
and T. E. Donald Dunkerly.
Presbytery, at its Adjourned Meeting on December I, 1979 in Panama City, voted to send all papers,
correspondence, and other materials dealing with the above named matters, together with the “ record of the
case ’' for the Lockman appeal to the General Assembly, as References to the General Assembly in accordance
with B.O.C.O. chapter 42. We send them for “ final disposition” (42-3).
It was Presbytery's feeling that the above matters met exactly the four criteria for such references:
"matters that are new, delicate, difficult, or on which the members of the lower court are seriously
divided.
Attest:
George M. McGuire
Stated Clerk of Gulf
Coast Presbytery
See § 8-13, 1; p. 62. December4, 1980

### G. RESOLUTIONS TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY

To the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures
Resolution 1: From RE G. O. Runnels and TE John S. Ragland

Whereas, on several preceding General Assemblies the Presbyterian Church in America affirmed in
faithful obedience to the Lord and Sovereign our Saviour Jesus Christ the 6th commandment's prohibition
against abortion on demand as presently practiced in this country resulted in the loss of more than 6,000,000
human lives in the past decade; and

Whereas, our Confessional subordinate standards make it very clear that God’s commandments com
mand specific things for God's people to doa swell as not to do; and

Whereas, our Larger Catechism in question 135, "What are the duties required in the sixth command
ment?" says, among other things, "The duties required in the sixth commandment are, all careful studies and
lawful endeavours, to preserve the life of ourselves and others by . . . comforting and succouring the distressed,
and protecting and defending the innocent."

Whereas, the Committee on Abortion report to the Sixth General Assembly recommended that we remind
all Christians of their duty to show compassionate love and understanding to families in distress as a result of
pregnancies, and to offer to these families sympathetic counsel and help for physical needs where required.
This duty is especially incumbent upon us as we minister to the person contemplating abortion.

Be It Therefore Resolved, that the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America
recommends to its churches that they make a concerted effort to develop positive ministries to those
considering abortions such as evangelism, Christian nurturing, Christian counseling, provision of financial
and material needs to the mother and her baby, aid with obtaining medical service, aid with adoption when
indicated, and Christian homes (homes for unwed mothers and Christian families who will share their home
with the pregnant woman in need of a place to live ora home away from their immediate family).

<a id="ga08-p54"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=54 printed_page=null -->

And That It Be Further Resolved, that this resolution be placed in the Messenger, and in a letter to all
the churches of the Presbyterian Church in America
TE John S. Ragland REG. O. Runnels
Bay Street Presbyterian Church Bay Street Presbyterian Church
Hattiesburg, Mississippi Hattiesburg, Mississippi
Grace Presbytery Grace Presbytery
Adopted as amended. § 8-69, III, 6; p. 99.
To the Committee of Commissioners on Administration
Resolution 2: From TE Harold Borchert
That General Assembly business be conducted annually during seven days from Wednesday to Wednes
day. Committee meetings to be held Monday and Tuesday with Sunday to be a day of rest and worship.
Harold Borchert
Southern Florida Presbytery
Answered in the negative. § 8-103, III, 25; p. 123.
Resolution 3: From TE Edwin P. Elliott, Jr.
that the Book of Church Order be amended so th a teach church be entitled to one elder representative at
presbytery and assembly for each 100 members or fraction thereof up to a maximum of 10 ruling elders from
any particular congregation.
Edwin P. Elliott, Jr.
Mid-Atlantic Presbytery
Answered in the negative. § 8-103, III, 26; p. 123.

Moderator Joseph called for the newly-elected moderator, TE Paul G. Settle, to
come forward for installation. He turned over the gavel and Mr. Settle assumed the chair.

RE Ralph M. Langford, chairman of the Committee on Administration, came
forward and presented a plaque and gavel to Retiring Moderator Joseph in recognition of
his service as moderator. Moderator Settle led the Assembly in prayer.

The moderator appointed RE W. Jack Williamson assistant parliamentarian for the
Eighth General Assembly.

The stated clerk and assistant parliamentarian reviewed procedures of operation of the
Assembly for the benefit especially of first-time commissioners.

gulf coast be found in order and placed in the hand sofa judicial commission
appointed by the Eighth General Assembly to report to the Ninth General Assembly, this commission to be given the authority to make final disposition
of the matter as requested by the Presbytery of Gulf Coast. It is recommended
that the General Assembly keep in mind the geographical location close at hand
to the presbytery in question in order to keep the cost within reason. We
nominate the following as the constituency of that commission:

8-19 Partial Report of the Committee of Commissioners on Administration
RE Edward Williford presented a partial report of the Committee of Commissioners
on Administration, beginning with prayer. The committee presented the following
recommendations:
1. That Overture No. 5 to the Eighth General Assembly from Evangel Presbytery,
be answered in the affirmative, amending the ‘‘Rules for Assembly Opera
tions” as follows:
a. Following the first sentence of Sub-section 8-11 (4) add the following
sentence:
‘‘The assembly may waive the reading of any particular report by a
majority vote of the commissioners present and voting.”
b. Following the second sentence of Sub-section 10-2, add the following
sentence:
“ The Assembly may waive the reading of any particular report by a
majority vote of the commissioners present and voting. ”
Adopted at the Stated Meeting of Evangel Presbytery, October 21, 1978.
Adopted.
2. That Recommendation No. 13 of the Committee on Administration be adopted,
suspending the ‘‘Rules for Assembly Operations” as follows:
That the “ Rules for Assembly Operation” be suspended in order that the
Eighth General Assembly may try a “ trial-run” on a new method of nomina
tions and elections, and that the following draft of rules be used by this
Assembly for the election of its permanent committees:
a. The nominations to the Assembly’s Permanent Committees and Subcommittees shall ordinarily be presented by the Assembly Nominating
Committee in the Commissioner’s Handbook. This presentation shall
include a brief statement regarding each nominee.
b. Additional nominations shall be made in writing on forms supplied by the
Stated Clerk, which shall include the consent of the nominee to serve, if
elected, and a brief statement regarding the nominee. a nominee is to give
consent to only one nomination. The deadline for these nominations is the
close of the afternoon session of the second day of the Assembly. The
clerk’s office shall issue a supplement to the Assembly Nominating Com

<a id="ga08-p69"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=69 printed_page=null -->

m ittee's Report during the third day’s business sessions,
c. Elections shall be held by the “ single transferable vote method.” Ballots
will be provided for each position, with a list of all nominees. Each
commissioner shall be asked to indicate his first, second, third, etc., choice
for each post. The ballots are then counted as follows: on the first count all
first choice votes are placed in separate piles and tabulated. If no nominee
receives a majority, the nominee with the smallest number of votes will be
declared out, and his pile of votes will be distributed according to the
second choice votes. if there is still no election, the lowest nominee is
again dropped, his ballots are distributed according to the next choice on
each ballot. If, after this procedure is carried out to the end, no one receives
a majority, the two top nominees shall be presented to the Assembly for a
final vote.
The time for the elections shall be docketed as a special order. Only those
commissioners present and on the floor of the Assembly shall be eligible to
vote. Adopted.
On motion the Assembly voted to delay the time for recess until after the report of
the Assembly Theological Examining Committee.

8-25 Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the World
TE Jack S. Ross, chairman, led in prayer and presented the report of the Committee
of Commissioners on Mission to the World.

#### I. Business Referred to the Committee.

1. Minutes of the Committee on Mission to the World June 18, 1979, September
7-8, 1979, November 15-17, 1979, February 14-16, 1980, May 17, 1980.
2. Audit Report for the Year Ended December 31, 1979.
3. Report of the Committee on Mission to the World to the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America (Appendix G, p. 187).

#### II. Major Issues Discussed.

1. Finances.
The fact that 41 percent of our missionaries were showing year-end deficits was
brought to the attention of the commissioners. This has happened in spite of the
fact that total income has increased 28.4 percent over 1978. The underlying
factors appear to be inflation and devaluation of the dollar.
2. Cooperative Agreements.
Three new cooperative agreements are reported to the Eighth General Assembly. One of these, with Overseas Crusades, Incorporated, was reported to have
theological language which was not in keeping with our standards. Accord
ingly, the Committee of Commissioners reviewed these agreements, with
particular emphasis upon the statement of belief of Overseas Crusades, Inc.
3 . Change of Policy Regarding Short-Term Missionaries.
Judging from the response of young people at Urbana and that which is being
found across the Denomination, a large number of young people would be
interested in a short-term assignment with Mission to the World. The interest
comes from both within and without the Denomination. To utilize this potential
would require changes in the Mission to the World “ Missions Manual". The
committee spent considerable time considering this matter.

#### III. Recommendations

1. That the minutes of the Committee on Mission to the World for June 18, 1979,
Septem ber7-8, 1979, November 15-17, 1979, February 14-16, 1980, and May
17, 1980, be approved. Adopted.
2. That the “ Audit Report forthe Y earEndedDecem ber31, 1979” be approved.
Adopted.
3. That the General Assembly express its gratitude for each of our missionaries
and join in prayer for God’s provision of every spiritual, emotional and physical
need in each of their lives. Adopted.
4. That the General Assembly give praise to God for His provision of an increas
ing number of church-planting candidates during 1979, and continue to pray
that God will “ send forth laborers into His harvest” . Adopted.
5. That the General Assembly re-elect TE Paul McKaughan as Coordinator and
the TE Kennedy Smartt as Coordinator of Church Relations for the Committee
on Mission to the World. Adopted.
6. That the Assembly express its appreciation to Missionary-Evangelist James L.
(Jimmy) Lyons and the entire MTW staff for their faithful and untiring service
on behalf of our missionaries and Mission to the World. Adopted.
7. That the Assembly express its appreciation for the faithful service of RE L. B.
(Pete) Austin III as chairman and RE Hugh W. Brown, Jr., and TE Eugene
Craven as members of the Committee on Mission to the World. Adopted.
8. That the third Sunday in May 1981 be approved as a day of self-denial and
prayer for world evangelization in general and our own Mission to the World
missionaries in particular. Adopted.
9. That the budget of Mission to the World for 1981, as presented to the Steward
ship Committee, be approved.
Deferred. Adopted in paragraph 8-80, p. 110).

<a id="ga08-p71"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=71 printed_page=null -->

10. That the General Assembly direct the Committee on Mission to the World to
review the Cooperative Agreement with Overseas Crusades, incorporated
( Appendix G, p. 195 ), for the purpose of defining items 4 and 7 under
“ What Does O.C. Believe?” . Adopted.
11. That the General Assembly authorize the Committee on Mission to the World to
create a structure that will enable students and those who are non-career
missionaries to respond to God’s call to short-term work worldwide.
Adopted.
12. That the Mission to the World Committee be authorized, for a two-year period,
to operate the Short-Term Project in exception to the Missions Manual in
Section 3.01.10 pertaining to PCA membership of Short-Termers*, and
2.02.1(4) and 2.02.2 pertaining to missionaries raising their own support.**
Quote from Missions Manual 3.01.10:
“ Church Relationship. Prior to approval, candidates will be expected to be
members of a congregation or presbytery of the Presbyterian Church in America.”
*This change would allow short-termers, who are in full accord with the PCA
standards, but are not necessarily members of the PCA, to serve with Mission to
the World.
2.02.1(4): “ Support. It is clear that the sending churches in the book of Acts
were involved in the support— prayer and financial— of their missionaries.
When a session or presbytery encourages an individual to mission service, it
accepts the responsibility to back up that person by prayer and giving. ’ ’
2.02.2 Enabling Committee (paragraphs 6 and 8):
“ It works with the missionary candidate and his church or presbytery in
planning for further training or experience where it is necessary. It assists
churches and presbyteries in the matter of support. It does not replace the
sending bodies in this responsibility but can and will assist congregations and
presbyteries, who desire assistance in the matter of support for their mis
sionaries, who do not have large support from their churches or presbyteries, to
find interested churches.
“ It recommends salary and benefit levels, assists the missionary in itineration
(in cooperation with session or presbytery) and helps him in the technical
matters related to his going overseas.”
**For career missionaries this responsibility is that of Mission to the World.
This change would give short-termers the responsibility of raising their own
support.
(Recommendation 12 is substituted for Recommendation 7 in the Report of
Committee on Mission to the World.) Adopted.

15. To accept the explanation given by Mission to the World below and approve its
action.
"Last year’s General Assembly in approving the minutes of the Committee on
Mission to the World, noted an exception in the case of Jakub and Esther
Susabda serving in an Indonesian Bible School, because there was no written
cooperative agreement between MTW and the agency under which the
Susabdas are serving. (See Assembly Minutes, 1979, p. 128, 7-68, III under
"Report” ). The Committee on Mission to the World was not asked for an
explanation by the Assembly at that time, but feels such an explanation is
needed:
a. Mr. Susabda is a graduate of Reformed Seminary, 1978, who has returned
to his homeland to teach in a Bible school there. he asked to be received by
MTW in order to receive the prayer support of the PCA.
b. Mrs. Susabda lacks only one year before completing her work on an M.D.
(medical doctor) degree. She is currently working on that.

<a id="ga08-p73"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=73 printed_page=null -->

c. The family is supporting itself or being supported by friends and family in
Indonesia.
d. If the school where Mr. Susabda is teaching signed an agreement with
MTW (a foreign organization), it would seriously jeopardize its privilege
of operation in a country that is extremely wary and defensive toward
outsiders intruding into the religious life of its people. (Missionaries are
being expelled.)
e - MTW sent one of its own missionaries to see the administrator of the
school and secured from him verbal concurrence to all the terms of our
cooperative agreement.
f. The administrator, not understanding why MTW was so insistent upon a
signature (which he felt would bring the government down upon his
school), wondered if MTW was not trusting a Christian brother, and why
MTW was making so much to do about supporting a Christian brother,
Jakub Susabda, with its prayer.
g. M TW ’s only financial commitment to Jakub Susabda is to channel such
funds as are specifically designated for his support. Adopted.
16. That the Report of the Committee on Mission to the World be approved as
amended. Adopted.
Respectfully submitted,
TE Jack Ross, Chairman
TE John Smith, Jr., Secretary

8-30 Committee of Commissioners on Ridge Haven
Moderator Settle called upon TE B. 1. Anderson to assume the chair for the ensuing
report. TE Richard A. Cumow, Jr., chairman of the Committee of Commissioners on
Ridge Haven, led in prayer and presented the committee's report.
I. Organization of the Committee
The Committee met at the Civic Center in Savannah, Georgia on Monday, June 16,
1980, at 8:30 a.m. RE Joseph Woodfield, the convener, called the meeting to order
and asked TE Paul Settle to open the meeting with prayer. TE Richard Cumow was
elected chairman. TE Samuel Hoyt, Jr. was elected secretary.
II. The committee reviewed the minutes of the Board of Directors of Ridge Haven, Inc.
All the members of the committee reported that they had read the report of the Board
of Directors. The introduction of this report was adopted as written. (See
Appendix J, p. 222.) The audit of the Board of Directors was received and the
committee was assured that the recommendations of the auditors are being imple
mented.

#### III. Recommendations

1. That the minutes of July 23, 1979; August 6, 1979; August 29, 1979; October
26, 1979; February 8, 1980; February 21, 1980; March 21, 1980; and April 28,
1980, be approved without exception. Adopted.
2. In order to clarify the method of filling unexpired terms of members of the
Board of Directors of Ridge Haven, Inc., that a section 3 be added to ARTICLE
V, Directors, of the Bylaws (M7GA, p. 268-9), to read:
3. Vacancies. A vacancy on the board of directors because of death, resigna
tion, removal, disqualification or otherwise, may be filled by the directors
for the unexpired portion of the term subject to the approval of the next
General Assembly,
and that the other sections in ARTICLE V be renumbered appropriately.
Adopted.

<a id="ga08-p77"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=77 printed_page=null -->

3. Approve RE Harrison R. King, Second Church. Greenville, SC, to fill the
unexpired term of TE Wayne Rogers, ’82, who resigned.
Adopted.
4. Approve RE Royce G. Waites, Northeast Church, Columbia, SC, to fill the
unexpired term of George Gulley, '82, who resigned. Adopted.
5. Approve TE Gordon K. Reed, Calvary Presbytery, to fill the unexpired term of
Pat T. Williams, '83, who resigned. Adopted.
6. That the Board of Directors give serious consideration to selecting qualified
persons from more distant areas in the temporary filling of future vacancies on
the Board. Adopted.
7. That The Presbyterian Church in America Foundation be authorized to borrow
up to $400,000.00 pledging the $800,000.00 note (payable in 5 equal annual
payments plus 6% interest) and the $200,000.00 note secured by the 1/3
interest in the Woodlawn Plaza Shopping Center mortgage due on or before
May 1, 1982, as collateral to provide Ridge Haven, Inc., with funds that will
enable it to proceed with construction of the first major building (Phase I
Lodge) at the earliest possible date. Adopted.
8. Elect RE Edward J. Robeson III as Administrator of Ridge Haven, Inc., to
serve in this capacity in accordance with the Bylaws and the Job Description
prepared by the Board. Adopted.
9. Express great appreciation to TE Gordon K. Reed for serving as Acting
Administrator of Ridge Haven, Inc. Adopted.
10. Express our sincere appreciation to the Women in the Church for their love gift
in 1980. Adopted.
Approve the amended budget for 1980 (p. 223).
Deferred. Adopted in § 8-80, p. 110.

Deferred. Adopted in § 8-80, p. 110.

8-35 Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities
Moderator Settle took the chair again, and the Assembly moved to consideration of
the report of the Committee of Commissioners on Insurance and Annuities. TE H.
Charles Green, J r., chairman, led the Assembly in prayer and presented the report.

#### I. Business Referred to the Committee

1. Minutes of the Board of Trustees.
2. Report of the Board of Trustees, Appendix B, p. 150.

#### II. Statement of Major Issues Discussed

1. The Minutes of the Board of Trustees meetings of June 18, July 20, November
20, 1979, and February 19, 1980, were reviewed.
2. Representatives of the Board appeared before the committee. Mr. Donald
Gaily, who will assist the Board as investment advisor, discussed his role and
explained the operation of the three investment firms who are currently han
dling the bulk of the assets of the Fund.
3. The Health Insurance program experienced a substantial increase in claims. As
a result, rates will be increased and the $100 deductible for out-patient service
will be reinstated.

#### III. Recommendations

1. That the Minutes of the Board meetings of June 19, July 20, November 20,
1979, and February 19, 1980, be approved without exception. Adopted.
2. That the Health Insurance Benefits be changed by extending the $100.00
deductible per person, $300.00 cumulative per family, to all medical services
except prescription drugs, additional accident care, and outpatient laboratory,
x-ray and diagnostic benefit, effective August I, 1980. Adopted.
3. That a $ 1.00 per month administrative fee be included in the Medical Insurance
Premium. Adopted.
4. That the Group Medical and Life Insurance Premiums for six months beginning
August 1, 1980, including administrative fee, be:
Employee only 41.00
Employee & 1 dependent 80.50 per month
Employee & more than 1 dependent 99.50 per month
Adopted.
5. That the Trustees be authorized to set the Health Insurance Premium for the
period 2/1/81 thru 7/31/81. Adopted.
6. That comparative prices be sought by our Trustees for the insurance program
prior to the 1981 General Assembly. Adopted.

<a id="ga08-p79"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=79 printed_page=null -->

7. That the General Assembly encourage all congregations to participate in the
pension plan on behalf of their ministers and lay employees. Adopted.
8 . That the General Assembly receive as information the Guidelines for the Relief
Fund adopted by the Trustees. Adopted.

8-36 Judicial Commission on Complaint of Byron Snapp and James Hope
against Calvary Presbytery
At 3:10 p.m. the moderator yielded the chair toT E Todd W. Allen. TE Rodney T.
King, chairman, led in prayer and presented the report of the Judicial Commission to
Adjudicate Case No. 3, “ Complaint of Teaching Elders Byron Snapp and James M.
Hope against Calvary Presbytery.’’ On motion the statement of the case and the
judgment rendered by the commission were approved and accepted by the Assembly as
its action and judgment on the case, and the whole was ordered spread upon the minutes.
Minutes of the Judicial Commission Appointed by the Eighth General Assembly to Adjudicate the Complaint of TE Byron Snapp and TE James M. Hope
Against Calvary Presbytery

<a id="ga08-p80"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=80 printed_page=null -->

The commission convened pursuant to the call of the convener June 16, 1980,
at 9:40 p.m. at the Savannah Civic Center, Savannah, Georgia.
A quorum was present with the following in attendance:
Teaching Elders Ruling Elders
Joseph H. Armfield Wilson J. Barbee
Frank Boswell A. H. Gibson
Ed Cunningham W. C. Hayes
William Hughes T. G. Melson, Jr.
Rodney T. King William J. Montgomery
Thomas Ramsay Fred Morris,
Thomas Rayside Henry G. Smith, Jr.
Thomas Roberts John G. Thompson
Steven Wilkins
Present, too, were Complainants Byron L. Snapp and James H. Hope; Respondent William Simoneau was appointed by the presbytery to defend the action of
presbytery.
The meeting was opened with prayer. On motion duly made, seconded, and
carried, TE Rodney King was elected chairman. On motion duly made,
seconded, and carried, TE Edwin Cunningham was elected secretary.
The chairman exhorted the commission in accordance with BCO 33-12, and
portions of chapters 33 and 43 of BCO were read for the instruction of the court.
The complete record of the case was read by the chairman. The complainants
made opening arguments and introduced, with permission of the respondent, a
written explanation and expansion of the argument. Respondent made opening
argument. Neither party desired to question the other. Members of the court
posed questions to both parties.
The court, by unanimous vote, went into executive session to discuss the merit
of the case and to express opinion.
The vote was then taken on the single specification of the complaint in the form
prescribed by BCO 43-7. The commission voted to sustain the specification of
error. The secretary and the chairman were directed to draw up a minute
explanatory of the action for perfection and adoption by the commission.
A motion was made, seconded, and carried, that the ordination be found
contrary to the Book of Church Order due to this error.
A motion was made, seconded, and carried, that this matter be remanded to
Calvary Presbytery for correction.
The following statement was adopted by the commission as the minute ex
planatory: ‘ ‘The Presbytery has not demonstrated that the use of the 'extraordi
nary clause' was justified by either extraordinary circumstances or proven
extraordinary gifts of the m an.”
A motion was made, seconded, and carried that the Sub-committee on Judicial
Business be directed to prepare an answer to the question, “ What is the proper
use of the extraordinary clause?", and report to the Ninth General Assembly
A motion was made, seconded, and carried to report these actions to the
complainants and to the respondent.
The minutes were perfected and approved. A motion was made, seconded, and
carried to approve the report as a whole.
A motion was made, seconded, and carried that the commission adjourn.
The meeting was adjourned with prayer.
Respectfully submitted,
Rodney T. King, Chairman
Edwin Cunningham, Secretary
Adopted.

Whereas, God in His providence called home our brother in the Lord, Robert
Strong while this Assembly was in session; and

Whereas, many of these commissioners remember with gratitude to God the life
and ministry of Dr. Strong as being a blessing in their personal lives; and

Whereas, Dr. Strong served his Lord with great humility and great effect within the
Church of Jesus Christ;
Now Be It Resolved, that the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America remember the life of our brother with praise to God and thanksgiving;
and further, that we convey our love and sympathy to the members of his family in
their time of bereavement. Adopted.

8-43 Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations

Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations.
I. Items Referred to This Committee

ruary 15. 1980.

<a id="ga08-p82"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=82 printed_page=null -->

#### II. Major Issues Discussed

1. A proposed relationship of the PCA to the Korean American Presbyterian
Church.
2. A proposed relationship of the PCA to the Reformed Ecumenical Synod.
3. Participation of the PCA in NAPARC's study of Hermeneutics.
4. The Permanent Sub-committee’s Recommendation 4 concerning an invitation
to other churches to join the PCA.
5. The work and report of the Ad-interim Committee to Discuss . . .
6. Communication 2 from the Orthodox Presbyterian Church and matters relating
to it.
7. An action of the Fraternal Relations Committee of the Reformed Presbyterian
Church, Evangelical Synod concerning their recommended response to their
General Synod to a possible invitation to join with the Presbyterian Church in America.
III. The following individuals met with and addressed the Committee of Commissioners
1. TE G. Aiken Taylor, chairman, Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations.
2. TE John P. Galbraith and TE Larry G. Mininger from the Orthodox Presbyterian Church.
3. TE Donald J . MacNair and RE Marion D . Barnes of the Reformed Presbyterian
Church, Evangelical Synod.
4. The following members of the PCA General Assembly: TE E. Crowell Cooley,
TE J. Philip Clark and TE Carl W. Bogue, Jr.

#### IV. Recommendations

1. That the minutes of the Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations dated October
2, 1979, and February 15, 1980, be approved with the following notations: The
members present were not designated as to their being ruling or teaching elders,
and the kind of meeting was not stated. Adopted
2. That the General Assembly at this time decline the invitation from the Korean
American Presbyterian Church.
Reason: The multiplicity of Presbyterian and Reformed groups in Korea and
among Koreans in this country suggests care to avoid any suggestion of
partiality. Adopted.
3. That in the interest of further information about the Reformed Ecumenical
Synod, the General Assembly authorize the attendance of two observers at the
Nimes meeting of the RES, these persons to be TE James A. Jones, Jr., andTE
William Edgar III.
Reasons: (1) The Seventh General Assembly decided not to join the RES at this
time.
(2) These PCA personnel are on the mission field in France and are
expected to be in Europe at the time of the meeting. Adopted.
4. That the General Assembly approve participation in a proposed NAPARC
study of the science of Hermeneutics, naming TE O. Palmer Robertson and TE
R. C. Sproul as PCA members of this study committee.
Reason: This study should benefit the PCA, especially in its understanding of
the positions of the other Churches in NAPARC. The two men named are
knowledgeable in the area and are willing to serve. Adopted.
5. That the Eighth General Assembly of the PCA reaffirm at this time that portion
of its original letter from our First General Assembly to all Churches, which
reads: "A s this new member of the family of Churches of the Lord Jesus Christ
comes into being, we necessarily profess the Biblical doctrine of the unity of all
who are in Christ . . . We greet all believers in an affirmation of the bond of
Christian brotherhood. We invite into ecclesiastical fellowship all who main
tain our principles of faith and order."

<a id="ga08-p83"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=83 printed_page=null -->

Reason: The Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations has responded to new
channels of discussion with other Churches of like confessional base for which
we are grateful. However, the Committee of Commissioners feels that the
substance of the letter proposed in the Sub-committee Recommendation 4 may
have been inappropriate in view of the actions of the Seventh General Assembly
(see M7GA, 7-34, Recommendation 5, p. 95).
Chairman Clements moved Recommendation No. 5. A motion was made and
seconded to substitute for Recommndation No. 5 the “ Letter” attached to Recommendation No. 4 of the Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations’ report (see p. 154),
excluding the text of Recommendation No. 4 itself.
A motion was made and seconded to amend the substitute so that the “ Letter”
would read as follows:
LETTER
to be adopted by the 1980 General Assembly
Presbyterian Church in America
To: The General Synods and General Assembly of the Reformed Presbyterian
Church, Evangelical Synod, the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North
America, and the Orthodox Presbyterian Church.
Subject: An invitation to effect one Church.
Brethren:
Greetings in the Names of the Lord Jesus Christ, the King and Head of the
Church.

Whereas, we hold to and desire to promote a common testimony to the
inerrancy of Scripture, the system of doctrine contained in the Westminster Confession of Faith and Catechisms, and the doctrine of the purity of the visible Church;
and

Whereas, we feel constrained by our commitments to seek a more perfect unity
among usa s members of Christ’s body;

Now Therefore, the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America,
in the bonds of our Lord Jesus Christ, invites you to come with us for the purpose of
effecting and perfecting one Church among us. We propose, as the basis of this
association, the above named principles, together with the Book of Church Order of
the Presbyterian Church in America.
Sincerely in Christ,
Paul G. Settle, Moderator
For the Presbyterian Church in America

RE Michael Williams led the Assembly in prayer.
Two commissioners asked questions related to the Constitution, and the moderator
referred these to the Sub-committee on Judicial Business. TE Thomas A. Cook,
vice-chairman, subsequently presented the following report on the questions.
Question 1. Does an invitation from the General Assembly to other ecclesiastical
bodies require a three-fourths vote of the presbyteries in order to be issued, on the
assumption that an invitation presupposes receipt of the body upon acceptance of the
invitation?
Response 1. The BCO does not speak to the issue of extending an invitation to other
ecclesiastical bodies but it does speak very clearly to receiving other ecclesiastical
bodies. It is the opinion of this sub-committee that the invitation could be extended
by the General Assembly without presbytery consent, but that in doing so the
General Assembly should remind those ecclesiastical bodies that their reception

<a id="ga08-p84"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=84 printed_page=null -->

would be contingent upon the consent of three-fourths of the presbyteries of the PCA
(BCO 15-6).
Question 2. What is the constitutional meaning of the phrase "the doctrine of the
purity of the church?"
Response 2. In responding to the question, the sub-committee has in mind the
statement in the fifth line of the “ Letter’’, which reads, " the doctrine of the purity of
the visible Church” . Such language is not found in the standards, but concern for the
purity of the visible Church is clearly expressed in Westminster Confession of Faith
25:4, 5, the “ Preface to the Book of Church Order” , 11(4), and Book of Church Order 2-1, 2-2, 22-5(6), and 25-5.
On motion this report was adopted by the Assembly.
[Clerk’s Note: This report was presented and adopted Wednesday morning (§ 8-52)
and is included here for easier reference.]
On motion the Assembly voted to go into a committee of the whole in closed
session, and rise without a report to continue until the body wishes to terminate the
posture of committee of the whole. The moderator named TE James E. Moore to chair
the committee of the whole.
[Extensive discussion ensued, and a "straw vote” was taken which favored
issuing an invitation to the RPCES and the OPC. The committee of the whole at
11:30 p.m . voted to rise to recommend to the eighth General Assembly of the
Presbyterian Church in America that we extend a simple invitation to the
RPCES and the OPC to consider matters necessary to effect church union with
us to the glory of christ and his Church. (Clerk’s Note: This material is not
actually part of the minutes of the Assembly, as this recommendation was never
received for consideration by the Assembly. It has been included for historical
reference and information.)]
The Assembly resumed regular session and voted to adopt the amendment on the
floor, by substituting the shortened form of the “ Letter” for the longer form originally
recommended by the Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations. The vote was 423
affirmative, 124 negative.
On motion the amended “ Letter" was further amended to add the following
paragraph between the last paragraph and the closing.
It is to be understood that this invitation is an action of the Eighth General Assembly, and to receive any denomination which responds to this invitation it
should be stated that for the Presbyterian Church in America to consummate any
such union, it would have to go through the constitutional process of approval by
subsequent General Assemblies and three-fourths of our presbyteries. In this constitutional process each denomination must be dealt with separately.
The amended substitute for Recommendation No. 5 of the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations was then adopted by vote of 525 affirmative, 38
negative.
On motion the Assembly voted to make copies of Recommendation No. 5, with the
vote tabulation, for commissioners to take home with them. The full letter in final form
follows.
LETTER
Adopted by the 1980 General Assembly
Presbyterian Church in America
To: The General Synods and General Assembly of the Reformed Presbyterian Church,
Evangelical Synod, the Reformed Presbyterian Church of North America, and the
Orthodox presbyterian Church.
Subject: An invitation to effect one Church.
Brethren:
Greetings in the Name of the Lord Jesus Christ, the King and Head of the Church.

<a id="ga08-p85"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=85 printed_page=null -->

Whereas, we hold to and desire to promote a common testimony to the inerrancy of
Scripture, system of doctrine contained in the Westminster Confession of Faith and
Catechisms, and the doctrine of the purity of the visible Church; and

Whereas, we feel constrained by our commitments to seek a more perfect unity
among usa s members of Christ’s body;

Now Therefore, the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America, in
the bonds of our Lord Jesus Christ, invites you to come with us for the purpose of
effecting and perfecting one Church among us. We propose, as the basis of this
association, the above named principles, together with the Book of Church Order of the
Presbyterian Church in America.
It is to be understood that this invitation is an action of the Eighth General Assembly, and to receive any denomination which responds to this invitation it should be
stated that for the Presbyterian Church in America to consummate any such union it
would have to go through the constitutional process of approval by subsequent General
Assemblies and three-fourths of our presbyteries. In this constitutional process each
denomination must be dealt with separately.
Sincerely in Christ,
Paul G. Settle, Moderator
For the Presbyterian Church in America
6. That the Ad-interim Committee to Discuss . . . be continued for one year and
that in the event approaches from any other Churches are made to the PCA
during the coming year, the Ad-interim Committee be authorized to welcome,
receive and study such approaches; be directed to communicate such informa
tion to the Church-at-large by all means available; and report to the Committee
of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations at the Ninth General Assembly of
the PCA.
Reasons: (1) The Committee of Commissioners was made aware of the follow
ing portion of the minutes of the Fraternal Relations Committee of the RPCES
which represents a recommendation of that committee, passed unanimously, to
the RPCES General Synod to meet in July, 1980, a copy of which was
forwarded to the PCA Sub-committee on Interchurch Relations for their infor
mation (see p. 155).
(2) The Committee of Commissioners also noted Communication 2
from the Orthodox Presbyterian Church. Adopted.
7. In response to Communication 2 from the 47th General Assembly of the
Orthodox Presbyterian Church, the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America take the following actions:
a. That the Ad-interim Committee continue to work on its original mandate,
and that they meet with the representatives of the OPC, and of the RPCES and
RPCNA, if the latter so desire, to draw up a statement that exhibits the
representatives’ understanding (or, if necessary, individual statements that
exhibit individual understandings) of the compatibility of the participating
Churches, the statement to take into consideration discussion of those questions
raised by PCA representatives at the joint meeting held September 14, 1979
(see p. 237), and any other pertinent issues. Adopted.

- **b.** That the Ad-interim Committee be instructed to report by means of a letter to all teaching elders and clerks of session no later than February 1, 1981, areas of similarity and difference among the PCA, OPC, RPCES and RPCNA, giving a brief summary of each Church’s position on these areas based on their standards and assembly pronouncements, along with a description of the size and location of the individual churches of each denomination. Adopted.
- **c.** That the Ad-interim Committee report to the Ninth General Assembly of the

PCA through the Committee of Commissioners on Interchurch Relations their

<a id="ga08-p86"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=86 printed_page=null -->

recommendations as to future efforts in the area of Church unity.
Reason: the Committee of Commissioners feels that this communication from
the OPC should be responded to positively, and that, as a special study
committee, the Ad-interim Committee is the proper vehicle to deal with these
discussions and make recommendations. Adopted.
8. That the stated clerk of the General Assembly be instructed to communicate
recommendations 5, 6 and 7 above to the stated clerks of the OPC, RPCES and
the RPCNA, noting also the procedures available in the PCA Book of Church Order, 15-6 and 27-4.
Reason: The Committee of Commissioners feels that it would be appropriate to
communicate officially our actions to these Churches. Adopted.
9. That Overtures 6, 18, 19, 28 and 33 be answered by referring to Recommendation 5 above. Adopted.
Respectfully submitted,
Don K. Clements, Chairman
Charles Howell, Secretary

8-50 Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the United States
The Committee of Commissioners on Mission to the United States reported through
the chairman, TE David F. Osborne, who began with prayer.

#### I. Business Referred to the Committee.

A . Minutes of the Permanent Committee on Mission to the United States.
1. 1979 (June 18, 21, 22; Sept. 6, 7; Decem ber7, 8)
2. 1980 (March 27-29)
B. Overtures:
1. Overture 10, From: Presbytery of Eastern Carolina.
(p. 40).
2. Overture 17, From: Pacific Presbytery, (p. 40).
3. Overture 20, From: Presbytery of Central Florida, (p. 41).
4. Overture 26, From: Session of Covenant Church, (p. 41).
5. Overture 30, From: Warrior Presbytery, (p. 42).
6. Overture 34, From: Mid-Atlantic Presbytery, (p. 42).
C. Report of Permanent Committee:
1. Reference Appendix F, page 173.

#### II. Major Issues Discussed.

A. The Five in Five Campaign. In view of the present status of the campaign, the
committee spent some time discussing proposed procedures with the M-US
Coordinator, The Reverend Philip Clark, and Mr. E. Allen Duble, acting
director of the campaign.
The most important matter before us was related to the recommendations
coming before the Assembly from the Permanent Committee. (Appendix F,
p. 173).
The proposal from the Permanent Committee, through the report of acting-
director Allen Duble, is that the Assembly act to authorize the 5-in-5 campaign
funds be setup as an endowment.
Note that in the Committee of Commissioner’s proposals to the Assembly there
is a change from the recommendation printed in the Report of the Permanent
Committee. Appendix F, p. 177.
B. Overtures concerning boundaries of existing presbyteries. The Committee of
Commissioners would like the Assembly to know that in our discussions of
Overtures and 34 (p. 42) we found an overwhelming approval of the overtures
by the presbyteries involved. It is the thinking of the committee that the General Assembly should respect this unanimity as from the Lord.
C. Overture 26, from Covenant Church of St. Albans, West Virginia (p. 41). The
committee, while viewing the Overture as not valid to be considered by this
Assembly, out of Christian courtesy to the parties involved, gave the floor to
the parties involved. The committee heard from TE Rod Mays, pastor of the
Covenant Session. After hearing their concerns, the committee heard from TE
Michael Bolus, Moderator of New River Presbytery and elected representative

<a id="ga08-p88"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=88 printed_page=null -->

of the presbytery to defend the presbytery’s action in defeating the Overture.
D. Request of the Permanent Committee for a one year delay in action on directive
of the Seventh General Assembly, in regard to the preparation of two manuals:
a policy m anual, and a Manual of Operations.
The Assembly will please note that the Committee of Commissioners has
amended the request of the Permanent Committee, a sit appears on page 174,
Recommendation 6, Appendix F.
The reasoning behind the Committee of Commissioners request to the Assembly is that the intent of the Seventh General Assembly for a separation of Policy
and Operations would not necessarily be accomplished by the one year delay as
presented by the Permanent Committee.
Please note in the body of the report that the Minutes of the Seventh General Assembly are referenced. These Minutes will show our concern, spoken by the
Seventh General Assembly, that the Permanent Committee compile two Manu
als: The first is to be a Policy Manual, pulling together all the actions of the
Assembly in establishing Policy: the second is to be a manual of operating
procedures, enacted by the Permanent Committee in fulfilling the Policy of the
Assembly. It is to be noted by the Assembly that the Committee of Commissioners in its request to the Assembly is asking the Permanent Committee to
complete the directive of the Seventh General Assembly, which will result in
two manuals.

#### III. Recommendations:

1. That the General Assembly approve the Minutes of June 18, 21-22, 1979.
Adopted.
2. That the General Assembly approve the Minutes of September 6-7, 1979.
Adopted.
3. That the General Assembly approve the Minutes of December 7-8, 1979,
with the noted exception that the Permanent Committee failed to submit
Attachments D, F, H, M, O with their Minutes to the Committee of
Commissioners. Adopted.
4. That the General Assembly approve the Minutes of March 27-29, 1980.
Adopted.
5. That the General Assembly answer Overture 10, (p. 40) from the Presbytery of Eastern Carolina, in the negative.
This overture is seen as unnecessary, since forms and information related
to this matter are now available. Also, it was felt that the present manner
helps to increase local initiative and involvement. Adopted.
6. That the General Assembly answer Overture 17, (p. 40) from Pacific
Presbytery, in the affirmative. Adopted.
7. That the General Assembly answer Overture 20, (p. 41) from the Presbytery of Central Florida, in the affirmative. Adopted.
8. That the General Assembly answer Overture 26, (p. 41) from the Session
of Covenant Church, in the negative.
This overture, as presented, was viewed as unconstitutional for this Assembly to consider, in view of Book of Church Order, Chapter 15-6, which
limits the power of the General Assembly in the realignment of presbyteries to their own consent, this overture being previously defeated by
New River Presbytery. Adopted.
9. That the General Assembly answer Overture 30, (p. 42) from Warrior
Presbytery, in the negative.
The term “ malcontent” was seen as not necessarily a bad term to apply to
many of us now in the Presbyterian Church in America, as to our former
denominational relationships. The committee did not agree that the tone of
the advertisement was negative in tone or intent. Adopted.

<a id="ga08-p89"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=89 printed_page=null -->

10. That the General Assembly answer Overture 34, (p. 42) from Mid-Atlantic
Presbytery, in the affirmative. Adopted.
11. That the General Assembly set aside Sunday, November 23, 1980, as a
special Day of Prayer and Thanksgiving for the Ministries of the
Assembly M-US Committee, and that a special offering be taken during
the Thanksgiving Season to go toward the work of our Ministries in New
England, that place where the first American Thanksgiving was held, and
which later became the center of the Great Awakening. We pray for a New
Awakening! Adopted.
12. That the General Assembly re-elect The Rev. J. Philip Clark as Coordi
nator of the Committee on Mission to the United States. Adopted.
13. That the General Assembly hear and act on the Permanent Committee’s
nomination of The Rev. Dwight Linton as Assistant Coordinator for
Special Ministries. Adopted.
14. That the General Assembly (at the appropriate time in the Assembly’s
agenda) approve the 1980 budget as presented by the Sub-Committee on
Stewardship, (p. 204). Adopted in Stewardship Report.
15. That the General Assembly approve the additions to the M-US Policy
Manual as presented in Appendix F, pp. 175-6, herein amended by the
Committee of Commissioners. Adopted.
16. That the General Assembly grant the M-US Committee one year to answer
the directive of the Seventh General Assembly to develop a Manual of
Operations and a Manual of Policy. (See copy below from Minutes of the
Seventh General Assembly, page 88, Item 6, par. “ C ” ). Upon completion,
the Policy Manual will be published in pamphlet form, available for use by
the General Assembly. The Operations Manual is not to be published for
General Assembly use, but is to be made available for inspection at any
time in the M-US office.
minutes of the seventh General Assembly. Report of the Committee of

Recommendation 6-C, pg. 88: ‘ ‘That the MUS prepare a revised policy
manual for approval by the Eighth General Assembly, and that MUS be

operation manual to be in conformity with the policy manual. These two
manuals shall be extractions from ail policy previously approved by all

D. That the M-US Committee appoint a group of professionally qualified men

and, to study and recommend farther alternate methods for making max
imum use of funds, in view of the eroding effects of inflation and the
present economic situation. Adopted.
E. That the General Assembly make the following change in the Five in Five
program, in view of the skyrocketing inflation upon the available funds:
A portion of the fund shall be administered as an endowment, with
loans being made for new church development from the interest
received on these investment funds.
The policy of Five in Five shall not allow for regular, undesignated gifts to
be placed in an endowment, but if donors designate their gifts to be placed
in an endowment, such designations shall be honored. Adopted.

8-63 Judicial Commission to Adjudicate Case No. 5
TE O. Palmer Robertson led in prayer and presented the report of the Judicial
Commission to adjudicate Case No. 5: Complaint of TE Carl W. bogue eta l against the
Presbytery of the Ascension. The Assembly voted to adopt the recommendation of the
Commission that the Minutes of the Commission be approved and accepted as the action
and judgment of the Assembly in this case.
Report of the Judicial Commission appointed by the Eighth General Assembly
to Adjudicate the Complaint of Carl W. Bogue et al,
as members of the Presbytery of the Ascension, Complainants
vs.
The Presbytery of the Ascension, Respondents
Statement of Facts
The pertinent facts which are not disputed are as follows:
1. On February 26, 1980, the Presbytery of the Ascension at a stated meeting
sustained the trials for ordination and approved the call to a campus ministry of
Mr. Sam Serio.
2. On March 3, 1980, teaching elder Carl W. Bogue et al, complained against
these actions of the Presbytery in writing, fulfilling the conditions of the BCO
44-4 and 43-4 that a complaint “ may be initiated if filed within fifteen (15) days
following the meeting of the court, with reasons supporting.”
3. The call of Mr. Serio by the Koinonia Christian Fellowship did not include in
writing an assurance that his work would afford “ the liberty to proclaim and
practice fully and freely the whole counsel of God, as contained in the Scrip-

<a id="ga08-p95"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=95 printed_page=null -->

tures and understood in the WCF," as required by the BCO 21-1.
4. The complainants and respondents indicated substantial agreement that in his
trial for ordination before the Presbytery, while indicating that he himself was
not practicing the matter under discussion, Mr. Serio:

- **a)** affirmed his belief that none of the gifts of the Spirit have ceased since the apostolic age.
- **b)** affirmed his belief that currently the gift of speaking in an unknown tongue, when interpreted by the gift of interpretation, communicates revelation from God, although the nature of the revelation involved was not clearly defined by Mr. Serio.

Statement of the Major Issue in Dispute
The major issue in dispute was whether or not Mr. Serio's statement concerning the
continuation of all the gifts of the Spirit, and the continuation of “ revelation" from God
were of such a nature that they substantially contradicted the fundamental teaching of the
WCF and BCO concerning the cessation of the extraordinary gifts of the Spirit, of gifts
related to revelation, and of the finalizing of revelation in Scripture.
Explanatory Opinion
1. The respondents concede as an error of oversight rather than an error of intent
that the Presbytery failed to conform to the requirements of the BCO 21-1
referred to above. This acknowledgment has the effect of providing specific
grounds for sustaining count 2 of the complaint.
2. The Commission judges that the Presbytery failed in allowing expressions
about continuing revelation by Mr. Serio to remain unclarified in the examination, so that the fundamental teaching of the WCF and the BCO concerning the
sufficiency and finality of revelation in Scripture was not adequately protected.
The Commission judges that simply affirming that the canon is closed, and that
supposed new revelations from God add nothing to the deposit of truth already
found in Scripture does not cover all the negations concerning continuing
revelation from God found in the WCF I, 1 ,6 , and the BCO 7-1. These
statements of the standards also negate the idea that any extraordinary ways still
continue in addition to Scripture as ways by which God verbally uncovers His
will to His people. According to the testimony of complainants and respon
dents, Mr. Serio affirmed belief in extraordinary revelation by tongues in
terpreted, while at the same time affirming that such revelation from God was
not to be added to the canon of Scripture.

Judgement of the Commission.
1. In balloting according to BCO 45, the Commission voted as follows:
To sustain the complaint: 10
Not to sustain the complaint: 0
To sustain the complaint in part: 5
of those voting to sustain the complaint in part,
0 indicated they were sustaining count 1, and
5 indicated they were sustaining count 2.
The combined result of the balloting was as follows:
To sustain count # 1 of the complaint: 10 yes, 5 no
To sustain count # 2 of the complaint: 15 yes, 0 no
2. The Commission remands this matter to the Presbytery of the Ascension to
secure-a proper call that conforms with the BCO 21-4.
3. The Commission remands this matter to the Presbytery of the Ascension to
re-examine Mr. Serio.

<a id="ga08-p96"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=96 printed_page=null -->

TE RE
O Palmer Robertson (Convener) C. E. Hornsby
Wayne Rogers Ken Ryskamp
Woody Markert Mike Minkoff
A1 LaValley Will Thompson
Bill Davies Jim Luce
Bruce Garris Don Kimsey
Tom Barnes C. J. Stender
Brister Ware Jimmy Mardis (Alternate)
Paul Lipe (Alternate)

DISSENT:
The undersigned dissent from the sustaining of Count 1 of the complaint on the
ground that the record is inadequate to support the findings of the majority. The minutes
of presbytery do not indicate the substance of the responses submitted by Mr. Serio
during the examination. There was no substantial agreement between the parties to this
cause as to the views of Mr. Serio. The undersigned fully concur in the theological views
expressed by the majority.
The undersigned also are concerned with the propriety of the call to support
ordination. The work contemplated by the call from the Koinonia Christian Fellowship
does not require ordination to the gospel ministry.
Kenneth L. Ryskamp
R. W. Markert
Paul Lipe (concurs in paragraph 1

8-69 Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures
RE Thurston Futch, chairman, led the Assembly in prayer and presented the report
of the Committee of Commissioners on Bills and Overtures.
I. Items referred to the Committee
A. Overture 32, p. 34
B. Overture 12, p. 33
C. Overture 2, p. 32

##### Overture 7, p. 32

##### Overture 27, p. 33

D. Overture 11, p. 32
E. Communication 1, p. 28
F. Resolution from TE John Ragland and REG . O. Runnells, p. 51..
II. Statement of Issues Discussed
A. There were several overtures dealing with thematter of abortion— Overtures 2,
7, 12, 27, pgs. 32 and 33. Inasmuch as allfour overtures were in substantial
accord, Number 12 was chosen to be considered first as representative of the
four.
B. Overture 11, p. 32 regarding the consumption of alcoholic beverages and the

<a id="ga08-p99"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=99 printed_page=null -->

resolution to declare “ in thesi” that total abstinence from alcoholic beverages,
except in medical use, be the approved position of our denomination in this
matter was discussed. The discussion by the members of the Committee was
representative of the various views and positions across our denomination. The
discussion also pointed out the difficult nature of resolving this issue within our
denomination to the satisfaction of everyone.
Recommendations
1. That Overture 32 be answered by referring the matter back to Grace Presbytery,
directing them to initiate a study of the matter regarding the proper recipients of
Christian baptism resulting in advice to particular churches with problems
regarding this matter and should there be a need, overture the General Assembly to amend the statements of our constitutional documents. Adopted.
2. That Overture 12 be answered in the affirmative with the following amend
ments:
a. That an editorial change be made under Section 4, line 3, by placing a
period after “ death” and that the following sentence begin with the words
"In such a case, the premature rem oval.
b. On the third line of the overture in the Handbook, delete the words
"Evangel Presbytery overtures the Eighth General Assembly to” and in
their place add “ that the Eighth General Assembly clarifies the action of
the Seventh General Assembly and” .
The Overture as amended is as follows:
"Overture 12: From Evangel Presbytery

WHEREAS, the General Assembly, as a court of jesus Christ,
should speak with a united voice in affirming the sanctity of human life
under the protection of the Sixth Commandment.

THEREFORE BE IT RESOLVED, that the Eighth General Assembly clarifies the action of the Seventh General Assembly and reaffirms the
statement of the Sixth General Assembly on abortion:
‘ ‘That because Scripture clearly affirms the sanctity of human life and
condemns its arbitrary destruction, we affirm that the intentional
killing of an unborn child between conception and birth, for any
reason at any time, is clearly a violation of the Sixth Commandment. ’ ’
Added to this statement are the following affirmations:
"Concerning crisis pregnancies in which it appears that the premature
removal of the unborn child from the mother is a necessary conse
quence of medical procedures essential to preserving the mother’s
life, we affirm that:
1. The Sixth Commandment not only forbids the taking of innocent
life for whatever reason, but also requires the preserving of
innocent life wherever possible.
2. The life of the mother as well as her child comes under the full
protection of the Sixth Commandment and all moral medical
wisdom and skill must be used to preserve her life as well as the
life of her child.
3. To say that we are ever placed in the position of choosing between
two sins (killing the child or neglecting the preservation of the
mother’s life) is to surrender our belief in the Sovereign overrul
ing providence of our All-wise and All-holy God (I Cor. 10:13),
and to allege that we must "do evil that good may come” . . . a
philosophy clearly condemned by Scripture.
4. An exception is not made even in the extremely rare case in which
in the judgment of competent medical authorities, the unborn
child’s continuing presence inside the mother's body will neces

<a id="ga08-p100"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=100 printed_page=null -->

sarily lead to the mother's death. In such a case, the premature
removal of the unborn child may be justified, provided that all
medical wisdom, judgment, and skill are used to preserve the life
of the child as well as the life of the mother. This premature
removal of the unborn child shall be at that juncture of time where
the greatest possibility for recovery is indicated for both mother
and child. If life is lost in such a case, and the death occurs not out
of criminal negligence, but merely out of the limitations of human
knowledge and skill, all has been done morally that could be
done. If we cannot save both lives, we are nevertheless morally
bound to save the life we can. ”
Grounds: The concern of the Sixth General Assembly was to stop
abortion. The concern of the Seventh General Assembly was to
preserve the life of the mother in crisis pregnancies. We believe
this overture as amended addresses and reconciles the concerns of
the two assemblies. Adopted.
3. That overtures 2, 7, and 27 be answered by reference to the action taken with
regard to Overture 12. Adopted.
4a. That Overture 11 be answered in the negative. (11-2).
Grounds: The grounds for answering this Overture in the negative are that
to adopt position of total abstinence would go beyond the requirements of
scripture, (Deut. 5:32,33; Col. 2:20-23) and is contrary to the Westminster Confession of Faith, (Chapter 20, subparagraph 2), which forbid the
binding of the conscience by the commands of men. Adopted.
4b. That the General Assembly adopt the following statement with regard to the
issue of temperance:
In answering Overture No. 11 in the negative the General Assembly
recognizes the problem of the abuse of alcoholic beverages in our society.
For this reason the General Assembly encourages local churches to:
(1) Teach and counsel as to the sin involved in the intemperate or escapist
use of any part of creation:
(2) Teach and counsel the kind of love and wisdom which may lead to
individual decisions to curb or to refrain from the use of a particular
aspect of the creation; and
(3) Proclaim and embody the reality of the work of the Holy Spirit in the
bond of vital fellowship within the body of Christ which is the biblical
antidote to the intemperance and escapism of our day. (cf. Ephesians
5:18, in context.) Adopted.
Affirmative votes for the following substitute for Recommendation 4 A, and B,
which substitute failed, were asked to be recorded as follows:
Substitute defeated: This General Assembly expresses its great concern
over the appalling price in terms of life, security, family, and property paid
by this generation as a direct result of the misuse of alcoholic beverages;
and commends as praiseworthy those who choose to make total abstinence
from alcoholic beverages a part of their Christian testimony before the
world.

5. That the communication from the Fairfield Church be acknowledged with
gratitude to our Lord Jesus Christ for the continued witness of this historic
church, and that we express our joy in the celebration of her tricentennial,
praying God’s continued blessing upon her for the future.
Furthermore, we ask the editor of “ The PCA M essenger” to consider publish
ing this letter. Adopted.
6. That the General Assembly adopt personal resolution No. 1 made by Teaching
Elder John Ragland and Ruling Elder G. O. Runnells, as edited and amended.
In subparagraph 5 after the words "concerted effort" add the clause “ to
support pro-life movements in their opposition to abortion and” . The edited
and amended resolution reads as follows:

WHEREAS, the Sixth and Seventh General Assemblies of the Presbyterian Church in America affirmed in faithful obedience to our Lord and
Sovereign Saviour Jesus Christ, the prohibition of the Sixth Commandment
against abortion on demand, which, as presently practiced in this country, has
resulted in the loss of more than 6,000,000 human lives in the past decade; and

WHEREAS, our Constitutional Standards clearly state that God’s com
mandments specify what God’s people are to do as well as not to do; and

WHEREAS, the Larger Catechism question 135 (“ What are the duties
required in the Sixth Commandment?” ) states, among other things, “ The
duties required in the Sixth Commandment are, all careful studies and lawful
endeavors, to preserve the life of ourselves and others by . . . comforting and
succouring the distressed, and protecting and defending the innocent.”

WHEREAS, the Report of the Ad-Interim Committee on Abortion to the
Sixth General Assembly recommends that all Christians be reminded of their
duty to show compassionate love and understanding to families in distress as a

<a id="ga08-p102"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=102 printed_page=null -->

result of pregnancies, and to offer to those families sympathetic counsel and
help for physical needs where required such duty being especially incumbent
upon us as we minister to the person contemplating abortion.

THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED that Eighth General Assembly of
the Presbyterian Church in America recommends its churches to make a
concerted effort in their opposition to abortion and to develop positive minis
tries to those considering abortions such as evangelism, Christian nurturing,
Christian counseling, and provision of financial and material needs to the
mother and her baby, aid with obtaining medical service, aid with adoption
when indicated, and Christian homes (homes for unwed mothers and homes of
Christian families who are willing to share their homes with a pregnant woman
in need of a place to live away from her immediate family).
AND THAT IT BE FURTHER RESOLVED, that this resolution be
placed in the PCA Messenger, and sent in a letter to the churches of the PCA.
Adopted.
7. On motion the report was received as a whole. Adopted.
On motion TE Charles W. McNutt was given the floor to express his conscience on
the matter of the Assembly’s answer to Overture 11. Adopted.
