STATEMENT OF FAITH:
We believe in the HOLY SCRIPTURES as originally given by God, divinely inspired, infallible, entirely
trustworthy; and the supreme authority in all matters of faith and conduct ONE GOD. eternally existent in
three persons: Father, Son, and Holy Spirit . . . our LORD JESUS CHRIST., God manifest me flesh. His
virgin birth, His sinless human life, His divine miracles. His vicarious and atoning death His bodily
resurrection. His ascension. His mediatorial work, and His personal return in power and glory the HOLY
SPIRIT, by whose indwelling the believer is enabled to live a holy life, to witness and work for die Lord Jesus
Christ . . . the UNITY OF THE SPIRIT of all true believers, the Church, the Body of Christ . . . the
RESURRECTION of both the saved and the lost; they that are saved unto the resurrection of life, they that are
lost unto the resurrection of damnation.

Exhibit B
COOPERATIVE AGREEMENT WHEREBY MISSION TO THE WORLD
MISSIONARIES OF THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA
WORK WITH OVERSEAS CRUSADES, INCORPORATED
THE TERMS OF THIS AGREEMENT RELATE TO THE CATEGORY OF A MEMBER MISSIONARY
RELATIONSHIP.
( I) The missionary will have dual membership status with both the Mission to the VWId and Overseas
Crusades, Inc.
( 2) The appointment of the missionary will be subject to the approval of both agencies in accordance with the
standards established by each agency.
( 3) In the event that one agency requests confidential materials gathered by the other, such materials will be
shared with the understanding that the materials will be kept confidential by that agency.
( 4) The missionary candidate will participate in the full candidate and training program of Overseas
Crusades, Inc.

<a id="ga08-p198"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=198 printed_page=null -->

( 5) Time will be allowed for the candidate to properly do itineration or deputation work under the
coordination of the Mission to the World within Presbyterian Church in America churches in order that
adequate prayer and financial support can be realized.
( 6) Overseas Crusades, Inc., will supervise the securing of visas and make other arrangements necessary for
beginning field work.
( 7) The Mission to the World will be the sponsoring agency for financial and prayer support of the
missionary.
( 8) Overseas Crusades, Inc., will be the directing agency in relation to missionary activities on the field.
( 9) Final discipline as relates to theology and morals rests in the proper church court of the Presbyterian Church in America.
(10) The Mission to the World missionary will have liberty in the full and free presentation of the gospel as
contained in and understood in the Reformed view, as contained in the Westminster Confession of Faith
and the Larger and Shorter Catechism, recognizing that he must also respect the position of others in an
interdenominational setting.
(11) While on the field and while traveling to and from the field, the missionary will be under the jurisdiction
of Overseas Crusades, Inc.
(12) While on the field, the missionary will be an integral part of the field staff sharing equally in privileges
and responsibilities as any other member and being subject to the policies and direction of the Overseas
Crusades,Inc.
(13) The missionary’s field director will initiate furlough planning in consultation with the Mission to the
World and also with the Overseas Crusades, Inc., U.S. Director.
(14) While on furlough, the missionary will be under the jurisdiction of Mission to the World. Among the
missionary’s furlough responsibilities, consideration will be given by the Mission to the World to
assignments, projects, additional study or training requested by Overseas Crusades, Inc. Progress and
activity information during furlough will be provided for Overseas Crusades, Inc.
(15) While on furlough, the missionary will be expected by Mission to the World to carry on a deputation
ministry for the Mission to the World within the constituency of the Presbyterian Church in America
congregations. Each agency will assume the arrangements and expenses of deputation when the member
is doing deputation for either agency. Primary deputation responsibilities will be within the Presbyterian Church in America under Mission to the World coordination.
(16) The missionary will not solicit homeland constituencies of either agency for personal funds or field needs
without the permission of the respective agency.
(17) The financial relationship of the missionary with Overseas Crusades, Inc., will be the same as that for all
other members including the assessment and support quotas, except that during any portion of furlough
under Mission to the World, the quota may be set by that agency. Mission to the World will receive and
receipt the missionary’s funds from the Presbyterian Church in America and transfer them to Overseas
Crusades, Inc., monthly to be transmitted to the field by that agency. Overseas Crusades, Inc., will
inform the Mission to the World of funds designated for the missionary from other sources.
(18) The hospitalization, retirement, and insurance plans provided by the Mission to the World will be
available to the missionary by mutual agreement of both agencies.
SIGNED:

Vice-President, Administration, Overseas Crusades, Inc.

President, Overseas Crusades, Inc.
DATE:

Chairman, Committee on Mission to the World, Presbyterian Church in America

Coordinator, Committee on Mission to the World, Presbyterian Church in America

What Does O.C. Believe?
Every member of the O.C. family subscribes to this Statement of Faith:
1. We believe that the Bible is the inspired Word of God and is infallible and authoritative in the original
writings.
2. We believe in one God, eternally existent in three Persons: Father, Son and Holy Spirit.
3. We believe in the deity of our Lord Jesus Christ, in His virgin birth, in His sinless life, in His miracles,
in His vicarious death and atonement through His shed blood, in His bodily resurrection, in His ascension to the
right Hand of the Father, and in His personal return in power and glory.
4. We believe that for the salvation of lost and sinful man, faith in the Lord Jesus Christ and regeneration
by the Spirit are essential.
5. We believe in the present ministry of the Holy Spirit, by Whose indwelling the Christian is enabled to
live a godly life.
6. We believe in the forgiveness of sins, the resurrection of the body, and life eternal.
7. We believe in the spiritual unity of the Church, which is the Body of Christ, composed of all who are
regenerated through faith in the Lord Jesus Christ.

NORTH AFRICA MISSION STATEMENT OF FAITH
I. The full inspiration of the Scriptures of the Old and New Testaments; their authority, sufficiency, and
inerrancy, not only as containing, but as being in themselves the Word of God; and the need of the
teaching of the Holy Spirit for a true and spiritual understanding of the whole
2. The unity of the Godhead and the divine co-equality of the Father, the Son and the Holy Spirit.
3. The utter depravity of human nature in consequence of the fall, and the necessity for regeneration.
4. The absolute Deity of our Lord Jesus Christ; His virgin birth; His real and perfect manhood; the authority
of His teaching, and the infallibility of all His utterances; His work of atonement for the sin of mankind by
His vicarious suffering and death; His bodily resurrection and His ascension into Heaven; His present
High-priestly intercession for His people; and His lordship over His church as its Supreme Head.
5. The justification of the sinner, solely by faith, on the ground of the merits and vicarious suffering, death,
and bodily resurrection of our Lord and Saviour, Jesus Christ.
6. The necessity of the work of the Holy Spirit in conviction of sin, regeneration, and sanctification, as well
as in ministry and worship.
7. The resurrection of the body; the judgment of the work by our Lord Jesus Christ; the eutrnal blessedness
of the righteous; and the eternal punishment of the wicked.
8. The personal return of the Lord Jesus Christ in glory.

Appendix H
REPORT OF THE
COMMITTEE FOR STEWARDSHIP MINISTRIES
TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY
OF THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA
The Sub-committee for Stewardship ministry is operating this year under new guidelines and re
sponsibilities which were approved by the last General Assembly. These guidelines include the following:
The committee continues to operate as a subcommittee of the Committee on Administration. It is
considered as a permanent sub-committee as to continuity, but it is not considered as a permanent
sub-committee as it relates to nominations and service.
The committee shall promote biblical stewardship at all levels of the church; and it shall be charged
with the responsibility of developing for, recommending to, and implementing for the General Assembly
systematic budgeting and finding procedures for all the General Assembly approved causes.
These responsibilities will be undertaken as the committee is able and willing to accept the
responsibility for funding them. Until such responsibility is accepted, the four permanent committees
will continue their responsibility in the manner assigned by previous General Assemblies.
Such budgeting and funding procedures are governed by the following rules:
(1) Committee budgets shall be divided into a “ committed'' and a “ growth" budget. “ Commit
ted " shall include all administrative and program commitments approved by the General Assembly
for this committee. “ Growth'' shall include those programs projected by the committee, approved
by the General Assembly, and which allow for the unusual demands and opportunities which
cannot be accurately envisioned during the budgeting process. Funding for such "growth” budget
shall be the responsibility of the Permanent Committee which proposes the same
(2) It is to be understood that the “ Growth” Budget is not to be a part of the “ Committed” Budget,
thus giving each committee the flexibility to project a high “ growth” budget not to be included in
the General Assembly's "askings” of the local churches.
(3) There will be no change in processing designated funds. All of the committees will continue to
receive gifts both "committed” and “ growth".
(4) All funds received by any of the four committees not designated as ' "growth” shall be assumed
to be “ committed” .
(5) Said four Permanent Committees shall be encouraged to submit revised budgets, if necessary, to
this committee prior to the General Assembly each year for submission to the General Assembly for
approval.
The committee to immediately embark on a system of “ askings” of each local church for the
support of the “ committed” budget of the four permanent committees. The committee will be funded as
an item in the “ committed” budget of the four permanent committees.
This committee will now review the budgets of the Committees and recommend an overall budget
to the General Assembly for its approval.
I. 1979 GIVING
A total of $3,506,826.00 was received by the four permanent committees of the General Assembly in
1979. This was the largest annual total yet for our PCA agencies The 1978 combined income of the four
committees was $2,959,706.00.
The Committee of Mission to the World received $2,200,000.00 in 1979, for 99% of its approved budget.
The Committee for the Mission to the United States received $623,000.00 09% ). Christian Education and
Publications received $412,000.00 (75%), and the Committee for Administration received $176,000.00
(79%). These increased percentages show a steady growth in the giving of our people to PCA causes,
even in the midst of inflation and yearly increased budgets by the Assembly. We believe
the efforts of the Stewardship Committee on behalf of the four committees are certainly reflected in the increase
of our churches.
The committee rejoices in the fact that total benevolent giving in 1979 increased 24.5% with the
percentage of disbursements allocated for PCA causes increasing by 36.3%. Non PCA causes increased
24.2%. Per capita giving to all causes increased from $458.29 to $505.04. An increase of 10.2%.
II. STEWARDSHIP NETWORK
The establishment of a stewardship network to facilitate communication of important information
between the program committees and the presbyteries is closing the communication gap in these presbyteries
that have Stewardship Chairman. These presbytery “ Key Men” receive a monthly update of vital information
concerning the four committees. These men in turn are responsible for communicating this information to the
local congregations and appropriate presbytery committees. The Key Man serves as a catalyst and as an
advocate for the General Assembly causes on the presbytery and local church level. As of this date, we have a
Stewardship Key Man in every presbytery within the denomination with the exception of one presbytery.
III. PRESBYTERY ASKINGS
At the direction of the General Assembly the Sub-committee for Stewardship Ministries calculated the
per capita contributions to the four permanent committees that would be necessary to meet their committed
1980 budgets. This information was distributed to each local church and the presbyteries with the request that

<a id="ga08-p202"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=202 printed_page=null -->

each church indicate the amount it plans to give to the work of the General Assembly. A summary of the
response of these churches is attached to this report.
IV. QUARTERLY FINANCIAL REPORTS
One of the most effective methods of keeping our pastors and sessions informed as to the financial status
of the four permanent committees has been the quarterly financial reports. These reports list income, percent of
income to budget, expenses (both program and administration expenses), and balance on hand for each of the
four committees.

### V. STEWARDSHIP SEMINARS

To assist local church officers, pastors and members in the preparation and implementation of an
effective stewardship program in the local church, your sub-committee continues to conduct Stewardship
Seminars. These one day seminars (usually held on a Saturday) consist of at least two general sessions and six
workshops. These seminars are a proven method of assisting local churches and the Assembly in the area of
stewardship. We have many letters on file in our office attesting to the success of these meetings. Time and
time again our records show that after the Stewardship Seminar the giving of the participating church to
General Assembly causes increases and in some cases there is a significant increase. Nearly 75 churches have
participated in these seminars since their inauguration in March of ’78.
VI. STEWARDSHIP MATERIALS
The Sub-committee continues to make stewardship materials available to our churches. In 1979, we
distributed over 132,000 pieces of literature in the form of tracts, pledge cards, and brochures to our people.
This was an increase of 43% over 1978. This year the Sub-committee introduces a new packet of material based
upon the theme "Stewardship Is You". Samples of these materials have been mailed to our churches and they
may be ordered from the stewardship office.
VH. 1980 CALENDARS
Your Sub-committee continues its efforts to publicize and assist in the coordination of Assembly,
presbytery and committee events through the publication and distribution of the Stewardship calendar. This
year the calendar contains printed dates (when information was available) of all presbytery meetings as well as
the regular meetings of the four permanent committees. This calendar was distributed to: each minister and
clerk of session in the denomination, each member of the General Assembly's permanent committees and each
committee staff person.
VIH.SPEAKER’S BUREAU
The Sub-committee further served the church through its Speaker's Bureau. This is a pool of layment who
are available for special messages on stewardship. These laymen filled the pulpit of several of the churches
across the denomination proclaiming God's stewardship message of time, talents and treasure. This service is
provided without cost to any church which desires a stewardship speaker.
IX. CASSETTE-NEWS
A special cassette-news tape was issued to each of our churches following the last General Assembly.
Written by one of the recording clerics, the cassette summarized the actions of the General Assembly. These
cassettes were distributed without charge to all our churches.

### X. REGIONAL CONFERENCES

Your Sub-committee organized and held "Vision 1979-80” Conferences in: Hattiesburg, MS and
Pittsburgh, PA. These are meetings where the four coordinators of the permanent committees present their
activities and plans. The conferences have been extremely well received and have provided the opportunity for
the leadership in local churches to gain first-hand information from the committee coordinators. The open
forum question and answer sessions have proven to be an important part of the "Vision 79-80” Conference.
XI. STATISTICAL SUMMARY
Your Sub-committee summarized and distributed the giving patterns of each of our churches and grouped
them according to size of membership. This information based upon the 1979 statistical reports indicated what
each church had received in total contributions, what amount was given to PCA causes (including presbytery)
and what was given to non denominational causes.
XII. BUDGETS
Operating under the new guidelines the committee reviewed each of the budgets of the other committees.
The guidelines used to review the budgets of these committees were as follows:
(1) Review the history of giving for each committee.
(2) Project from that history what could be expected for the coming year.
(3) Add a faith percentage to the figure derived in step #2.
Attached to this report are copies of these budgets which we are submitting to the Assembly for its
approval.
RECOMMENDATIONS
1. That the 1981 budgets be approved as submitted.
2. That the period of Sunday, October 12, 1980, through Sunday, November 2, 1980, be a special
stewardship season and Sunday, November 2, 1980, be recommended as Commitment Sunday.
3. That presbytery encourage each local church to appoint a stewardship Key Man.
4. That presbyteries encourage each church to participate in a Stewardship Seminar when it is offered in
their area.
5. That each church be encouraged to use the 1980 stewardship materials “ Stewardship Is You".
6. That churches and presbyteries be urged to complete the report on the 1980 Assembly askings as soon as
possible.

<a id="ga08-p203"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=203 printed_page=null -->

7. That the report on the statistical summaries be received as information.
8. That the Stewardship Sub-committee be funded by the four permanent committees.
9. That the PCA Foundation be funded by the four permanent committees.
10. That the asking procedure begun in 1980 be continued each year.

Appendix I
REPORT OF THE
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY
OF THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA
The Presbyterian Church in America Foundation was established by the Fourth General Assembly.
ostensibly it operates as a sub-committee of the Committee on Administration. However, the Fourth General Assembly which adopted the Charter and Bylaws for the Foundation took no action to amend the Bylaws of the
General Assembly to properly set out the relationship of the Foundation to the denomination. Such an
amendment would have been required in order to give the Foundation the proper nexus with the General Assembly. It is anticipated that the report of the Committee on Administration to the Eighth General Assembly
will contain necessary Bylaw amendments to properly delineate the status of the Foundation. Heretofore the
Foundation has been operating autonomously, reporting directly to the General Assembly with its affairs
Povemed by an eight-man Board of Trustees set out and established by the Charter and Bylaws of the
oundation. Each trustee is elected by the General Assembly to serve for a four-year term. Although the
Bylaws of the Foundation state that “ the terms shall begin with their election by the General Assembly and
shall end with the election of their successor by the General Assembly ’’, the Foundation as a matter of practice
has considered its trustees to serve for calendar year terms. Therefore, a trustee elected at the Seventh General Assembly in June, 1979, would have his term begin January 1, 1980, and continue through December, 1983.
Prior to the 1981 budget request, the Foundation has raised its operating funds outside of the General Assembly budget. In 1979 because of difficulties in raising the funds necessary to continue its operations on a
full scale basis, the trustees curtailed operations effective October 1, 1979, reduced its staff, adopted a revised
budget for the remainder of 1979 and the calendar year 1980. It was determined at the time that a total of $8,000
would be needed to operate for the remainder of 1979 and 1980 on the curtailed basis. At that time, the
Executive Committee of the Foundation's trustees presented the situation to each of the four General
Assembly’s permanent committees. Each Committee was requested to contribute $2,000 to sustain the
operations of the Foundation through the calendar year 1980. Subsequent to the annual meeting of the trustees
held November 10, 1979, at which this plan was approved, certain designated gifts were received by the
Foundation, were held for temporary periods and invested with substantial earnings. These earnings together
with the subsidies received from the four General Assembly committees have permitted the Foundation to
continue in operation through the time of the 1980 General Assembly and the Lord willing through the
remainder of 1980.
The trustees at their annual meeting on November 10, 1979, decided that the future operation of the
Foundation beginning in 1981 would require employment of a new full-time director. The trustees felt that such
a director would need to have considerable skills in fund raising. To this end a proposed 1981 budget of
$89,000 was adopted. This proposed budget, a copy of which is attached to this report, was submitted to the
Sub-committee on Stewardship. The Sub-committee on Stewardship subsequently took action to reduce the
budget of the Foundation, particularly the compensation package for the director, as indicated by the report of
the Sub-committee on Stewardship.
A search committee of the Foundation was appointed with the following responsibilities:
A. Prepare job description for the proposed new director.
B. Prepare profile of the man to be chosen for this position.
C. Be prepared to recommend such a man by the next meeting of the Trustees providing the General Assembly approves the proposed budget and mode of operations.
The search committee has been active in carrying out its responsibilities and has prepared such a profile
and job description for the proposed new director. It has also prepared a proposed "Plan for Operation” , a copy
of which is attached. Depending on approval of its budget and plans by the General Assembly, the search
committee will begin an active search for a full time director immediately following the Eighth General Assembly, with the goal of employing someone for the position beginning January 1, 1981.
RECOMMENDATIONS:
1. That the proposed 1981 budget of $89,000 as requested by the Board of Trustees be approved;
2. That the approved budget for 1981 be allocated to each of the four General Assembly Committees in the
ratio of their sharing of undesignated gifts to the General Assembly as set out by the Eighth General Assembly;
3. That the Bylaw changes proposed by the Committee on Administration affecting the Foundation be
approved.
4. That each church in the Assembly be encouraged to utilize the services of the Foundation in promoting
planned and deferred giving within their membership;
5. That the General Assembly consider that coordination and supervision of all fund raising be
assigned to the Foundation as proposed in the attached "Plan for Operations.”
PLAN FOR OPERATION
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
FOR 1981
It is anticipated that the PCA Foundation will be the primary organization responsible for planned giving
programs for the entire denomination. Planned giving would include deferred and capita] fund giving.

<a id="ga08-p215"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=215 printed_page=null -->

It is further proposed for consideration by the General Assembly that all fund raising come under the
supervision of the Foundation with the Director responsible for coordinating the efforts carried on within and
by each General Assembly Committee or any other arm of the church including Ridge Haven. The Subcommittee for Stewardship would be dismantled and the functions it now serves transferred as follows:
1. Education in Christian Stewardship including the development of materials for use by the local
church to the Committee on Christian Education and Publications;
2. Receiving, compiling and transmitting information relative to per capita giving to the Committee
on Administration;
3. Review and approval of Committee budgets to the Committee on Administration.
The Foundation will continue to operate for the balance of 1980 on a curtailed basis under the part-time
direction of Mr. M. E. Howland, Director of the Sub-Committee on Stewardship. A full-time director would
be employed to be effective January 1, 1981. Prior to his employment date, it is anticipated that a survey would
be made of the potential for deferred and planned giving within the constituents of the PCA and its friends at
large in the Christian community. An outside consulting service would be utilized for this purpose. From this
survey, five year goals for the program of the Foundation would be set accordingly. The setting of these goals
would be coordinated with the new director and would receive his agreement prior to adoption by the
Foundation trustees.
It is anticipated that the office of the Foundation would be moved to Atlanta, Georgia near the offices of
the three General Assembly committees already situated in Decatur, Georgia. As the Foundation would be
responsible for all capital funds drives, (and possibly all fund raising) it would be necessary that the Foundation
office have good communication with the General Assembly Committees. Attorneys for the Assembly and the
Foundation are located in Atlanta.
The Director would operate in an office of 350-500 square feet of floor space, allowing room for a private
office, a secretarial office, a file room and expansion room for an assistant. He would be provided with a leased
automobile and an adequate telephone and travel budget to accomplish the goals of the organization.
It is anticipated that a portion of the budget of the Foundation would be covered by direct gifts received
for the support of the Foundation as well as earnings made on temporary investments of gifts received by the
Foundation designated for other PCA agencies or for other donnees authorized by the charter of the
Foundation. The balance of the Foundation's budget would be incorporated in the budgets of the four operating
committees of the Assembly on a pro-rata basis, based on the sharing of undesignated gifts set by each General Assembly. The budget anticipated for 1981 and requested of the Sub-Committee on Stewardship is $89,000.

PROPOSED BUDGET
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
FOR 1981

MINORITY REPORT
THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY
The Word of God sets forth very clearly that the stewardship of time, talents, and possessions is the
responsibility of every individual Christian. The basis of stewardship is the blessing of God as recognized by
grateful hearts. David, in his prayer which he offered when the materials for the temple had been gathered,
gives us the expression of grateful stewardship. "Now therefore, our God, we thank thee, and praise thy
glorious name. But who am I, and what is my people, that we should be able to offer so willingly after this sort?
For all things come of thee, and of thine own have we given thee. For we are strangers before thee, and
sojourners, as were all our fathers. Our days on earth are as a shadow, and there is none abiding. O Lord our
God, all this store that we have prepared to build thee an house for thy holy name cometh of thine hand, and is
all thine own. I know also, my God, that thou triest the heart, and hath pleasure in uprightness. As forme, in the
uprightness of my heart I have willingly offered all these things: and now have 1seen with joy thy people .which
are present here, to offer willingly unto thee. " I Chron. 29:13-17.
Since the basis of stewardship is the blessing of God, the responsibility of teaching and encouraging
stewardship must rest with the individual congregation, and thus the admonition of Scripture must be obeyed.
“ Every man according as he purposeth in his heart, so let him give; not grudgingly nor of necessity: for God
Ioveth a cheerful giver. And God is able to make all grace abound toward you; that ye, always having all
sufficiency in all things may abound to every good work: Being enriched in everything to all bountifulness,
which causeth through us thanksgiving to God.” 1 Cor. 9:7,8,11. The instructions of Scripture will preclude
any attempt on the part of the church to be a financial institution.
Attention of the Assembly is called to certain irregularities in the operation of the Board.
1. The meeting of the Board held November 10, 1979, was held without a quorum; therefore, all
actions taken at that meeting are null and void.
2. Notice for the meeting included these words, “ As you are aware, we are running a deficit in our
operating funds. Therefore, we trust that you will be able to make your own arrangements to cover
your travel expense." This definitely contributed to the fact that there was not a quorum present.
The undersigned do not believe that the Assembly expects committee members to do the work of the
Assembly at their own expense.
3. The report printed in the Handbook was never presented to the Board for consideration and is,
therefore, not properly before the Assembly.
4. Recommendations 6, 7, 8, and 9 in the supplement to the handbook were never considered by the
Board.
RECOMMENDATIONS
1. That the budget for the Foundation be set at thirty thousand dollars ($30,000) for 1981.
2. That the operation of the Foundation be placed under the Assembly's Committee on Administration
(similarly to that of the Board of Insurance and Annuities) and that the budget for the Foundation be added to
that of the Committee on Administration.
3. That the By-laws of the Corporation be amended to restore the review of the several budgets of the
committees to the Committee on Administration, Section 7-22, par. 3 to read "the Committee on Stewardship
Ministries" to “ Committee on Administration."
4. That the Foundation be relieved of any responsibility for promoting planned giving.
5. That the General Assembly reaffirm the statement of purpose of the Foundation as it is found in the
Manual, minutes of fourth General Assembly, p. 198, Article I, Purpose: The first sentence which reads.
“ The Foundation is established to receive, accumulate, manage, invest, and disburse capital funds entrusted to
it."
SUPPLEMENTAL REPORT OF THE
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY
OF THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA
Additional Recommendations:
6. Amend the Rules for Assembly Operations Section 8-1 of Article VIII to delete item 12 under the
heading of ' ‘Committees".
7. Amend the Rules for Assembly Operations Section 9-1 of Article IX to delete item (5) now reading
“ Stewardship" and renumber (6) and (7) to (5) and (6).
8. That the By-Laws be amended to delete Section 10, of Article IV.
9. That the second sentence of Section 3 of article iv of the By-Laws be amended to read as follows:
‘‘The budget for each Permanent Committee, Ridge Haven and the PCA Foundation shall be
submitted to the Committee on Administration, which shall consider the requests of each
submitting committee or organization as it relates to the budget ■ requests of the other
Committees, including its own and shall recommend budgets for each submitting committee
or organization and its own budget to the General Assembly.

Attachment A ARTICLES OF INCORPORATION
OF THE
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION
I.
The name of the Corporation is: Presbyterian Church in America Foundation.
n.
The Corporation is organized pursuant to the provisions of the Georgia Nonprofit Corporation Code.
III.
The Corporation shall have perpetual duration.
IV.
The Corporation is organized solely for the following purposes:
(a) To receive, accumulate, manage, invest and disburse any assets, or income therefrom, received by
gift, bequest, devise, transfer in trust, or other conveyance, with a view to using such assets for the support of
the cause of the Kingdom of Jesus Christ, primarily through the Presbyterian Church in America, but also
through other groups, societies, organizations, and institutions which minister in Jesus' name to man's
spiritual, physical, emotional, and intellectual powers;
(b) to carry on, conduct, promote, operate, and undertake any transaction, operations, or activities
commonly carried on, conducted, promoted, operated, or undertaken by non-profit organizations engaged
exclusively in religious, charitable, and educational activities within the meaning of Section 501(c) (3) of the
Internal Revenue Code of 1954 (or the corresponding provision of any future United States Internal Revenue
Law) including, for such purposes, the making of distributions to such organizations;
(c) to do everything necessary for the accomplishment of the foregoing purposes, and to do all other
things incidental to them or connected with them that are not forbidden by the Gc»rgia Nonprofit Corporation
Code, by other law, or by these articles of Incorporation; and for any other lawful purpose not specifically
prohibited to nonprofit corporations under the laws of Georgia.
V.
The Corporation shall have no members.
VI.
The Board of Directors of the Corporation shall be elected by the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America. Only members of the Presbyterian Church in America may serve as directors of the
Corporation. The initial Board of Directors shall be:
Class of 1984
Andrew Trotter, Robert Brown
Class of 1983
John Albritton, James Wasson
Class of 1982
James E. Moore, Steve A. White
Class of 1981
Laurie V. Jones, Robert Baxter
VII.
No part of the net earnings of the Corporation shall inure to the benefit of, or be distributable to, the
directors or officers of the Corporation or to other private persons, except that the Corporation shall be
authorized and empowered to pay reasonable compensation for services rendered and to make payments and
distributions in furtherance of the purposes set forth in Article IV hereof. No substantial part of the activities of
the Corporation shall be the carrying on of propaganda, or otherwise attempting, to influence legislation, and
the Corporation shall not participate in, or intervene in (including the publication or distribution of statements)
any political campaign on behalf of any candidate for public office. Notwithstanding any other provision of
these articles, the Corporation shall not carry on any other activities not permitted to be carried on (a) by a
corporation exempt from federal income tax under Section 501 (c) (3) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954 (or
the corresponding provision of any future United States Internal Revenue Law) or (b) by a corporation.

<a id="ga08-p218"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=218 printed_page=null -->

contributions to which arc deductible under Section 170 (c) (2) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954 (or the
corresponding provision of any future United States Internal Revenue Law).
VIII.
Upon the dissolution of the Corporation, the Board of Directors shall, after paying or making provisions
for the payment of all of the liabilities of the Corporation, distribute any assets held by the Corporation upon
condition requiring return, transfer, or other conveyance, which condition occurs by reason of the dissolution,
in accordance with such requirements. All remaining assets shall be distributed to such organizations and
institutions as are selected by the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America, provided,
however, that such selection shall include only organizations which qualify as exempt organizations under
Section 501(c) (3) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1954 (or the corresponding provision of any future United
States Internal Revenue Law), and whose purposes and activities are not inconsistent with the purposes of this
Corporation.
IX.
The initial registered office of the Corporation shall be 2500 Peachtree Center, Cain Tower, 229
Peachtree St., NE, Atlanta, Georgia 30043 and the initial registered agent of the Corporation at such address
shall be Henkel & Lamon, P.C.
X.
The name and address of the incorporators is Thomas F. Leopard, 3001 US Highway 280, South,
Birmingham, Alabama 35243 and W. Jack Williamson, Box 467, Greenville, Alabama 36037.
IN WITNESS WHEREOF, the undersigned executes these Articles of Incorporation this 1st day of
August, 1980.
J. Austin Thompson, Jr.
For: Henkel & Lamon, P C.
Attorneys for Incorporator

Attachment B BY LAWS OF
THE PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION, INC.
ARTICLE I
MEMBERS
The Corporation shall have no members.
ARTICLE D
DIRECTORS
2.1 General Powers
The business and affairs of the Corporation shall be managed by its Board of Directors. The Directors
shall in all cases act as a Board, and they may adopt such rules and regulations for the conduct of their
meetings and the management of this Corporation as they may deem proper, not inconsistent with these
Bylaws and the laws of Georgia.
2.2 Specific Powers

- **a.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to solicit, receive and accept gifts, devises, or bequests of all forms of property, both real and personal, tangible and intangible, or the income therefrom, outright or in trust, from any individual, corporation or other organization, subject to such retained interest and other conditions which may be agreed upon by the transferor and the Board or specified in the instrument of conveyance.
- **b.** Except as limited by any instrument of conveyance or agreement between the transferor and the

Board of Directors, and except as otherwise provided in paragraph (c) of Section 2.2 hereof, the
Board shall exercise complete and exclusive discretion with respect to the investment, reinvest
ment, disposition, and control of any property, or income therefrom, transferred or conveyed to the
Corporation.

- **c.** The ultimate disposition or distribution of any property or income received by the Corporation, other than transfers which are required by any instrument of conveyance or other agreement between the transferor and the Board of Directors, of which represent the exercise of the authority of the Board to manage and invest such property and income, shall be determined in the manner ordered and directed by resolution of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America.
- **d.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to borrow money for such purposes as are consistent with the purposes of the Corporation as stated in the Articles of Incorporation, on such terms and from such sources as the Board considers proper, and to mortgage or pledge any property held or administered by the Corporation for uses not inconsistent with the purpose for which the money borrowed is to be spent.
- **e.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to loan money for such purposes as are consistent with the purposes of the Corporation as stated in the Articles of Incorporation, on such terms and subject to such security as the Board considers proper.
- **f.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to combine any separate fund or property with any other fund or property for convenience of administration and investment, and for such purposes to hold such several funds in one or more common accounts in which separate funds have undivided interests.
- **g.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to employ agents, employees, counsel, and such other personnel as the Board considers necessary, and to delegate to them such powers as the Board considers proper.
- **h.** The Board of Directors shall have the power to pay all reasonable costs, charges, and expenses incurred in the administration of the property of, and income received by, the Corporation, including compensation to persons referred to in paragraph (g) of Section 2.2.

2.3 Number, Term, and Qualifications
The number of Directors of the Corporation shall be eight (8). Each member of the Board of Directors
must be either a Teaching Elder, Ruling Elder, or Deacon in the Presbyterian Church in America. At least
two of the Directors shall be Teaching Elders and at least four shall be Ruling Elders or Deacons. Each
Director shall be elected for a term of four (4) years; provided, however, that the initial Board of Directors
shall be elected for the following terms; Two (2) Directors shall be elelected for a term of one (1) year;
two (2) Directors shall be elected for a term of two (2) years; two (2) Directors shall be elected for a term
of three (3) years; and two (2) Directors shall be elected for a term of four (4) years. No Director shall be
eligible for reelection to the Board until one years after his or her term expires; provided, however, that if
a director has served fora term of less than four (4) years, he or she shall be eligible for immediate
reelection at the end of such term. There shall be no limit on the number of terms which a Director may
serve. The members of the Board of Directors shall, upon assuming office, immediately enter upon the
performance of their duties and shall continue in office until their successors shall be duly elected and
qualified. The Managing Director of the Corporation shall serve as an additional member of the Board of
Directors in an advisory capacity only and shall not have the right to vote.

<a id="ga08-p220"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=220 printed_page=null -->

2.4 Election of Directors
Directors shall be elected by a majority vote of the members of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America in accordance with the Bylaws, the Rules for Assembly Operation, and the Book of Church Order of the Presbyterian Church in America. Nominations for the Board of Directors shall be
presented to the General Assembly by the nominating committee of the Presbyterian Church in America.
2.5 Vacancies
Whenever any vacancy occurs in the Board of Directors by reason of the death, resignation, or removal
from office of a Director, the vacancy shall be filled at the next subsequent annual or special meeting of
the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America in accordance with the election procedures
set forth in Section 2.4.
2.6 Removal
Any Director may be removed from office prior to the expiration of his or her term, with or without cause,
by a majority vote of the members of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America.
2.7 Compensation
Directors shall not receive salary for their services as Directors; but, by resolution of the Board, expenses
of attendance may be allowed for attendance at each meeting of the Board. A Director may serve the
Corporation in a capacity other than that of Director and receive compensation for the services rendered
in that other capacity, and no individual shall be precluded from serving the Corporation in another
capacity or receiving compensation therefore by reason of being a Director.
2.8 Officers of the Board of Directors
the board of directors shall appoint by a majority vote a Chairman, Vice-Chairman, and Secretary from
among the members of the Board to serve as Officers of the Board. These Officers shall serve at the
pleasure of the Board of Directors and shall have such duties as may be prescribed by resolution of the
Board or by these Bylaws.
2.9 Executive Committee
The Chairman, Vice-Chairman, and one other Director appointed by a majority vote of the Board of
Directors shall serve as the Executive Committee of the Board to perform the duties of the Board during
such time when the Board is not in session. All actions of the Executive Committee shall be submitted for
ratification at the next subsequent meeting of the Board, or the actions may be submitted to the individual
members of the Board for ratification by mail. Any action of the Executive Committee which the Board
fails to ratify shall be declared void ab initio. No ratification shall be required, however, if the power to
take such action was previously delegated to the Executive Committee by resolution of the Board of
Directors.
2.10 Other Committees
The Board of Directors shall appoint from among its members and others such committees as the Board
may deem necessary or advisable for the proper operation of the Corporation.

ARTICLE III
MEETINGS OF DIRECTORS
3 .1 Place of Meetings
The meetings of the Board of Directors may be held at the registered office of the Corporation, or at any
place within or without the State of Georgia that a majority of the Board of Directors of the Corporation or
the members of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America may from time to time by
resolution designate, or that may be designated in any notice of a meeting.
3 .2 Annual Meetings
A meeting of the Board of Directors shall be held at least annually, and no notice of such meeting, other
than that provided by these Bylaws, shall be required.
3 .3 Special Meetings
Special meetings of the Board of Directors may be called by or at the request of the Chairman, or by any
three or more Directors, or by direction of the members of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America
3.4 Notice
Written notice of each annual or special meeting of the Board of Directors, setting forth the time, place,
and date of the meeting, shall be mailed to each member of the Board of Directors at least ten (10) days
before the time appointed for the meeting. Such notice shall be given either by hand delivering a copy or
sending a cppy through the United States Mail. If mailed, such notice shall be deemed delivered when
deposited in the United States Mail, addressed to the Director at his address as shown in the records of the
Corporation, with first class postage thereon prepaid.
3.5 Waiver of Notice
notice of a meeting need not be given to any director who signs a written waiver of notice either before or
after the meeting; and a Director's waiver shall be deemed the equivalent of giving proper notice.
attendance of a director a ta meetings hall of itself constitute a waiver of notice of such meeting, and a
waiver of any and all objections to the place of the meeting, the time of the meeting or the manner in
which it has been called or convened, except where a Director states at the beginning of the meeting any
such objection or objections to the transaction of business.

<a id="ga08-p221"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=221 printed_page=null -->

3.6 Quorum
a majority of the directors shall constitute a quorum for the transaction of business at any meeting. If a
quorum is present, the affirmative vote of a majority of the Directors in attendance shall be the act of the
Board of Directors and all resolutions adopted and all business transacted by the Board shall require the
affirmative vote of a majority of the Directors present at the meeting. When a quorum is once present to
organize a meeting, it is not broken by the subsequent withdrawal of any of those present. if a quorum is
not present, a majority of the directors present may adjourn the meeting to a later date.
3.7 Presumption of Assent
a director who is present a ta meeting of the board of directors shall be presumed to have concurred in
any action taken at the meeting, unless his dissent to such action shall be entered in the minutes of the
meeting, or unless he shall submit his written dissent to the person acting as the Secretary of the meeting
before the adjournment of the meeting, or shall forward such dissent by registered or certified mail to the
Secretary of the Corporation within 24 hours after the adjournment of the meeting. Such right to dissent
shall not apply to a Director who, being present at the meeting, failed to vote against such action.
3.8 Action by Consent
any action which may betaken a ta meeting of the directors may betaken without a meeting if a written
consent, which may be in the form of minutes of a meeting, setting forth the action so taken, shall be
signed by all of the Directors.

ARTICLE IV
OFFICERS
4.1 Titles of Officers
the corporations hall have a managing director and a Secretary. Such other officers and assistant
officers as may be deemed necessary may be elected or appointed by the Directors. One person may be
elected to more than one office, except that the offices of Managing Director and Secretary may not be
held by the same person.
4.2 Election
The Officers of the Corporation shall be elected by the Board of Directors at the annual meeting of the
Board. Each Officer shall be elected for a term of one (1) year, which term shall commence on the day of
election at the annual meeting of the Board of Directors. Each Officer shall hold office until his successor
shall have been duly elected and qualified, or until his death, resignation, or removal from office.
4.3 Removal and Vacancies
Any Officer elected by the Directors may be removed by the Directors whenever, in their judgment, the
best interests of the Corporation would be served thereby, but such removal shall be without prejudice to
the contract rights, if any, of the person so removed. Election or appointment of an Officer shall not, of
itself, create contract rights. A vacancy in any office occuring for whatever reason may be filled by the
Directors for the unexpired portion of the term at an annual or special meeting of the Board.
4 .4 Managing Director
The Managing Director shall be the principal executive officer of the Corporation and, subject to the
control of the Directors, shall supervise and control the business and affairs of the Corporation. He may
sign, with the Secretary or any other proper officer of the Corporation authorized by the Directors, any
deeds, mortgages, bonds, contracts, or other instruments which the Directors have authorized to be
executed, except in cases where the signing and execution thereof shall be expressly delegated by the
Directors or by these Bylaws to some other officer or agent of the Corporation, or shall be required by law
to be otherwise signed or executed. He shall (i) have charge and custody of and be responsible for all
funds and securities of the Corporation, (ii) receive and give receipts for moneys due and payable to the
Corporation from any source whatsoever, and (iii) deposit all such moneys in the name of the Corporation
in such banks, trust companies or other depositories as shall be selected by the Board of Directors If
required by the Directors, the Managing Director shall give a bond for the faithful discharge of his duties
in such sum and with such surety or sureties as the Directors shall determine. He shall, in general,
perform all other duties incident to the office of Managing Director and such other duties as from time to
time may be prescribed by the Board of Directors
4.5 Secretary
The Secretary shall maintain custody of the corporate records and the Seal of the Corporation and, in
general, perform all duties incident to the office of Secretary and such other duties as from time to time
may be prescribed by the Board of Directors. The Chairman of the Board of Directors shall serve as the
Secretary, unless a Secretary shall have been duly elected by the Board of Directors.
ARTICLE V
ECCLESIASTICAL MATTERS
The Ecclesiastical Constitution of the Presbyterian Church in America is composed of the Westminster Confession of Faith, the Larger and Shorter Catechisms as adopted by the General Assembly of the

<a id="ga08-p222"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=222 printed_page=null -->

Presbyterian Church in America, and the Book of Church Order of the Presbyterian Church in America. The
provisions of the Ecclesiastical Constitution shall take precedence over any provisions of these Bylaws which
may be in conflict therewith.

ARTICLE VI
INDEMNIFICATION
6 .1 Determination of Indemnification Right
a. the corporations hall indemnify any person who was or is a party or is threatened to be made a party
to any threatened, pending or completed action, suit or proceeding, whether civil, criminal,
administrative or investigative (other than an action by or in the right of the Corporation) by reason
of the fact that he is or was a director, officer, employee or agent of the Corporation, or is or was
serving at the request of the Corporation as a director, officer, employee or agent of another
corporation, partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise, against expenses (including
attorneys’ fees), judgments, fines and amounts paid in settlement actually and reasonably incurred
by him in connection with such action, suit or proceeding if he acted in a manner he reasonably
believed to be in or not opposed to the best interests of the Corporation, and, with respect to any
criminal action or proceeding, had no reasonable cause to believe his conduct was unlawful. The
termination of any action, suit or proceeding by judgment, order, settlement, conviction, or upon a
plea of nolo contendere or its equivalent, shall not, of itself, create a presumption that a person did
not act in a manner which he reasonably believed to be in or not opposed to the best interests of the
Corporation, and, with respect to any criminal action or proceeding, had reasonable cause to
believe that his conduct was unlawful.

- **b.** the corporations hall indemnify any person who was or is a party or is threatened to be made a party to any threatened, pending or completed action or suit by or in the right of the Corporation to procure a judgment in its favor by reason of the fact he is or was a director, officer, employee or agent of the Corporation, or is or was serving at the request of the Corporation as a director, employee or agent of another corporation, partnership, joint venture, trust or other enterprise against expenses (including attorneys' fees) actually and reasonably incurred by him in connection with the defense or settlement of such action or suit if he acted in good faith and in a manner he reasonably believed to be in or not opposed to the best interests of the Corporation and except that no indemnification shall be made in respect of any claim, issue or matter as to which such person shall have been adjudged to be liable for negligence or misconduct in the performance of his duty to the Corporation unless and only to the extent that the court in which such action or suit was brought shall determine upon application that, despite the adjudication of liability but in view of all the circumstances of the case, such person is fairly and reasonably entitled to indemnity for such expenses which the court shall deem proper.
- **c.** Any indemnification under paragraph (a) or (b) of Section 6.1 (unless ordered by a court) shall be made by the Corporation only as authorized in the specific case upon a determination that indemnification of the director, officer, employee or agent is proper in the circumstances because he has met the applicable standard of conduct set forth in paragraphs (a) and (b). Such determination shall be made (1) by the board of directors by a majority vote of a quorum consisting of directors who were not parties to such action, suit or proceeding, or (2) if such a quorum is not obtainable, or, even if obtainable, if a quorum of disinterested directors so directs, by independent legal counsel in a written opinion, or (3) by the members of the General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America, by a majority vote of a quorum consisting of those members who were not parties to such action, suit or proceeding.
- **d.** To the extent that a director, officer, employee or agent of the Corporation has been successful on the merits or otherwise in defense of any action, suit or proceeding referred to in paragraph (a) or (b)

of Section 6.1 orin defense of any claim, issue or matter therein, he shall be indemnified against
expenses (including attorneys’ fees) actually and reasonably incurred by him in connection
therewith.
e. The provisions of this Article shall also apply to members of any committee or subcommittee of the
Corporation.
6.2 Payment
A disinterested majority of the Board of Directors of this Corporation shall be authorized to pay to any
person entitled to indemnification under this Article all actual expenses incurred in connection with such
action, suit or proceeding during the pendency thereof, upon the receipt of an undertaking by or on behalf
of such person to repay such amount, unless it shall ultimately be determined that such person is entitled
to be indemnified by the Corporation as authorized in this Article.
6.3 Intent
It is the intention of the Corporation that this Article of the Bylaws of the Corporation and the
indemnification hereunder shall extend the maximum indemnification possible under the laws of
Georgia, and if any one or more words, phrases, clauses, sentences, paragraphs, or sections of this
Article should be held unenforceable for any reason, all remaining portions of this Article shall remain in
full force and effect.

<a id="ga08-p223"></a>
<!-- PAGE ga=8 pdf_page=223 printed_page=null -->

ARTICLE VD
AMENDMENTS
These Bylaws may be amended or repealed and new bylaws may be adopted by a majority vote of the
Board of Directors at any annual or special meeting.
ARTICLE VIII
APPROVAL OF BYLAWS
Neither these Bylaws nor any amendment or alteration hereto shall become effective until approved by a
majority vote of the members of the General Assembly at any annual or special meeting.
ARTICLE IX
MISCELLANEOUS
9 .1 Seal
The Seal of the Corporation shall be in such form as the Board of Directors may from time to time
determine, and shall initially be in the following form:
PRESBYTERIAN CHURCH IN AMERICA FOUNDATION, INC.
CORPORATESEAL
GEORGIA
In the event it is inconvenient to use such a seal at any time, the signature of the Corporation, followed by
the word "SEA L" enclosed in parentheses or scroll, shall be deemed the Seal of the Corporation. The Seal
shall be in the custody of the Secretary and affixed by him or any assistant secretary on such papers as may be
directed by law, by these Bylaws, by the Managing Director, or by the board of Directors. The presence or
absence of the Corporate Seal on any instrument, or its addition thereto, shall not affect the character, validity,
or legal effect of the instrument in any respect.
9.2 Registered Office
The initial address of the registered office and name of the registered agent of the Corporation are stated in
the Articles of Incorporation. The registered office and registered agent of the Corporation may be
changed from time to time by the Board of Directors. The Corporation may establish offices at such other
place or places both within and without the State of Georgia as the Board of Directors may from time to
time determine.
9.3 Headings
The Article and Section headings contained herein are for convenience and reference only, and shall in no
manner be construed as a part of these Bylaws.

# Appendix J
## REPORT OF RIDGE HAVEN CONFERENCE CENTER TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY

### I. INTRODUCTION

Ridge Haven, your Conference Center is in the process of moving from a concept to a reality. The rate of this development, albeit slow, has accelerated significantly during this past year. The limited facilities we have been able to develop are in full use with a schedule of activities extending even into the next calendar year.

We are still a long way from having a fully developed Conference Center, and we desperately need the opportunity to present this cause in all of the congregations of the Presbyterian Church in America. The response to our presentation so far has been encouraging, but the failure of large numbers of our churches to honor our request for such presentations has been disappointing. The obvious difference between interest and disinterest is the degree of co-operation which we receive from the pastors.

During the past year we have been the recipient of a number of contributions and within the past few months have been informed of one large gift that will amount to approximately one million dollars over a period of five years.

At the present time we have built a mini-lodge which will accommodate forty people comfortably. It is a home with cooking and meeting facilities as well as both private and dormitory space for sleeping. The picnic shelter is complete with lights and water and tables for forty. We are continuing some of the basic work now, such as road, sewerage, water, and electricity for the entire complex. Since all our utilities will be underground, it is necessary to get them in place before too much building is done. The engineering studies on the dam will soon be complete, and we hope to have the dam built this summer.

Plans are underway to begin work on another guest house and the family camping area this summer. We would like to have two houses, the lake, the utilities, and some camping space finished by fall.

The architects are working on the drawings for the Phase One Lodge which will become part of the Study Center eventually. If sufficient funds were available we could begin construction of that building this coming year. The rate of development of the Conference Center from this point on will depend upon the gifts of congregations and individuals within the Presbyterian Church in America, since we may only proceed as the money is in hand. We hope that enough people in the Church will show an active and generous interest in Ridge Haven to enable us to build and maintain a Conference Center which will serve the Lord and His Church.

### II. RECOMMENDATIONS TO THE EIGHTH GENERAL ASSEMBLY OF THE PCA

The Board of Directors of Ridge Haven, Inc., recommends that the Eighth General Assembly of the Presbyterian Church in America:

1. Hear the Report of Ridge Haven, Inc.
2. In order to clarify the method of filling unexpired terms of members of the Board of Directors of Ridge Haven, Inc., that a section 3 be added to Article V, Directors, of the Bylaws (page 268-269, Minutes of the Seventh General Assembly of the PCA, 1979) to read:
3. Vacancies. A vacancy on the board of directors because of death, resignation, removal, disqualification or otherwise, may be filled by the directors for the unexpired portion of the term subject to the approval of the next General Assembly.
4. and that the other sections in Article V be renumbered appropriately.
5. Approve Harrison R. King, ruling elder, Second Church, Greenville, S.C., to fill the unexpired term of Wayne Rogers, ’82, who resigned.
6. Approve Royce G. Waites, ruling elder, Northeast Church, Columbia, S.C., to fill the unexpired term of George Gulley, ’82, who resigned.
7. Approve Gordon K. Reed, teaching elder, Calvary Presbytery, to fill the unexpired term of Pat Williams, ’83, who resigned.
8. Approve an annual appeal for funds for Ridge Haven, Inc., in the MESSENGER since Ridge Haven is the only major ministry in the PCA not in the general budget.
9. Authorize the Presbyterian Church in America Foundation to borrow up to $400,000.00 pledging the $800,000.00 note (payable in 5 equal annual payments plus 6% interest) and the 50% interest in the Woodlawn Plaza Shopping Center mortgage due May 1, 1982, as collateral to provide Ridge Haven, Inc., with funds that will enable it to proceed with construction of the first major building (Phase I Lodge) at the earliest possible date.
10. Elect Edward J. Robeson, III, as Administrator of Ridge Haven, Inc., to serve in this capacity in accordance with the Bylaws and the Job Description prepared by the Board.
11. Express great appreciation to Gordon Reed for serving as Acting Administrator of Ridge Haven, Inc.
12. Approve the amended budget for 1980. (See Attachment A.)
13. Approve the amended budget for 1981. (See Attachment A.)
14. Approve the Report as a whole.

Appendix K
MINUTES OF ASSEMBLY’S
THEOLOGICAL EXAMINING COMMITTEE
The Theological Examining Committee met December 27, 1979, at 1:00 p.m. in the Hartsfield
International Airport, Atlanta, Georgia, members present were: The Rev. James Bland, Mr. George Calhoun,
Mr. Da De Lange, The Rev. David Osborne, alternate voting as principal. After convening with prayer, the
committee proceeded to examine The Rev. Dwight Linton, Assistant Coordinator designate for The M-US
committee, in the areas of personal experience, theology, the sacraments, and church government. Following
this, a motion was unanimously passed sustaining The Rev. Linton’s satisfactory examination. A second
motion was passed, recommending to the Assembly that The Rev. Linton be approved as Assistant Coord
inator to M-US.
The meeting was adjourned with a season of prayer.
Respectively submitted,
David Osborne, Clerk

The Assembly’s Theological Examining Committee met March 13, 1980, at 1:00 p.m. in the Hartsfield
International Airport, Atlanta, Georgia. Members present were: The Rev. James Bland III, The Rev. Douglas
J. Culver, The Rev. Bob Vincent, Mr. George Caihoun, and the Rev. David Osborne (alternate). After Bob
Vincent opened the meeting with prayer, the committee proceeded to examine Mr. Ed. Robeson, administrator-designate for Ridge Haven, in the areas of personal experience, theology, sacraments, and church
government. Following this, a motion was unanimously passed sustaining Mr. Robeson’s satisfactory
examination.
In addition, the committee passed a motion recommending to the Assembly that Mr. Robeson's
examination be approved for the position as Administrator of Ridge Haven.
There being no further business the meeting was adjourned with a season of prayer.
Respectively submitted,
David Osborne, Clerk
